The National Salvation Donation Investigation Committee Sent a Letter Yesterday Requesting Various Courts to Report 103

The Review Committee Announced that the Minor Details of the Report Are on File for Review

The Shanghai All Circles Investigation Committee for National Salvation Donations, due to the discovery of corruption in the anti-Japanese donations, sent a letter yesterday requesting the courts to report and notified the donors, fundraising organizations, and recipients of funds to immediately report to the committee for verification. The details are as follows:

Requesting the Courts to Report The committee sent a letter yesterday requesting the procuratorates of various courts to report. The original letter stated, "Dear Sirs, Recently, newspapers have been spreading rumors about the embezzlement of anti-Japanese national salvation donations. Your offices are responsible for inspection, and for this case, you should, regardless of whether it is based on rumors, automatically investigate and report based on your duties. However, it has been two weeks since the matter, and we have not yet seen any indication from your office, which is deeply surprising. General Li Du has now publicly stated that Mr. Zhu Qinglan has committed serious corruption in the anti-Japanese national salvation donations. Upon hearing this, we were even more shocked. We hereby formally request your office to report Mr. Zhu Qinglan and seal and safeguard all income and expenditure account books and receipts of the anti-Japanese national salvation donations that he has handled, and warn Mr. Zhu not to leave Shanghai without authorization before the case has been fully investigated, so as to facilitate the investigation and clarify the truth. This has been decided at the third committee meeting of our association. We hereby send this letter and hope that you will investigate and handle it and reply to us. Respectfully, To the Shanghai District Court, Shanghai First Special District Court, Shanghai Second Special District Court, Procuratorate."

Announcement by the Review Committee The Specialist Review Committee of the association announced yesterday to all donors, fundraising organizations, and remittance organizations that if they have received donation funds, they should report to the committee. The original text stated, "The Shanghai All Circles Investigation Committee for National Salvation Donations has approved the organization of a specialist review committee at the third committee meeting to facilitate the review work, and nominated Xi Yushu, Lu Zhaozuo, Pan Qizhang, Xie Lin, Qin Kai, Jiang Wanfeng, Yu Xizhi, Li Wenjie, and Xia Sunhuan as members of the specialist review committee. He Yuanming and Wang Haifan, the heads of the review section, are ex officio members, etc. This national salvation donation is a righteous act of our countrymen. Since the society has doubts about the amount and purpose, the members of this committee, who are also accountants, have been entrusted with the task of detailed review to clarify the truth. However, review requires accounts and evidence in order to be effective. Therefore, we are publishing this announcement. Donors of national salvation donations are requested to report the amount donated at that time, where the funds were handed over, and what receipts were obtained. If the funds were directly remitted to the recipient of the donation, please report which bank or firm remitted the funds, to whom and where they were remitted, and what receipts were obtained, so that we can verify them. Fundraising organizations are requested to report the name and amount of the donation, which bank or firm remitted the funds, to whom and where they were remitted, and what receipts were obtained, and send a list to this committee. If a credit record has been published, please also send it. If donation expenses are paid out of the donations, please include them. Remittance organizations are requested to report the amount of national salvation donations remitted, where the funds were entrusted to be remitted, to whom they were remitted, and what receipts were obtained, so that this committee can verify them. Recipients of donations are requested to report the amount of donations actually received, from which place and fundraising organization they were remitted, and which bank or firm they were received from, so that this committee can verify them. Furthermore, we welcome any opinions from the people regarding the review methods. This announcement is hereby made. The Specialist Review Committee. Address: Shanghai Accountants Association, No. 4 Hong Kong Road, Shanghai."

The General Affairs Office of the Military Council's Shanghai Office is Ordered to Close 104

According to the Central News Agency, the Military Council, due to the urgent war situation in North China, and the people from all walks of life, motivated by patriotic enthusiasm, have donated a constant stream of comfort items, for the convenience of receiving and transshipping these comfort items, the General Affairs Office's Shanghai Office was specially established, and Li Dachao, a section chief of the municipal government, was appointed as its director. Since its establishment, the work has been extremely tense. At present, the war in North China has come to an end, and there are no more comfort items to be received and transshipped. New Ning-Shao Resumes Service 108

The Ning-Shao Company's "New Ning-Shao" steamer has been undergoing extensive repairs in dock since it was taken out of service on the 23rd of last month. After more than twenty days, all the passenger accommodations on the ship have been completely renovated. The berths have been made more comfortable, and the food has been made particularly exquisite, hoping to satisfy passengers. The repairs have now been completed, and the ship is scheduled to resume its Shanghai-Ningbo service on Monday, the 21st of this month.

Postal Workers' Union Held Oath-Taking Ceremony Yesterday 109

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union held its 11th Executive and Supervisory Committee oath-taking ceremony at the China Thrift and Virtue Society yesterday at 9 a.m. Tao Baichuan of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Wang Xiaolai of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Xie Baochen of the Postal Administration, Jaffe Lin and Dai Baohua of the Shanghai Postal Administration, Lu Jingshi of the National Postal Workers' General Union, Ye Xianggao of the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, Wang Wenqing of the Customs Club, Yu Zhenhui of the Municipal Farmers' Association, Mao Yun of the Second Municipal Council, representatives from various trade unions, and more than 500 representatives and members from various branches of the Executive and Supervisory Committees attended. The Postal Workers' Military Band played music at the venue, and Boy Scouts and police officers from the Public Security Bureau maintained order. The details of the conference are recorded below.

Chairman's Report 110

The conference nominated Ke Chang, Lu Keming, and Shui Xiangyun as the presidium. After performing the rituals, Chairman Zhang Kechang first reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that today's meeting has two meanings: one is the oath-taking of the 11th Executive and Supervisory Committees, and the other is the celebration of the 8th anniversary of the union's founding. Recalling this day eight years ago, postal workers felt unfair treatment and suffered various oppressions and pains, so they united to seek their own liberation. After the first major strike, the Postal Workers' Union was declared established. We have observed that the past ten committees have been able to devote themselves to union affairs with a spirit of sacrifice, and as a result of the support and supervision of all members, the union's current situation has been created. The current Executive and Supervisory Committees, at the beginning of their term, should bear the heavy responsibility entrusted by the members, uphold the spirit of practicality, diligence, and hard work, and strive to achieve the essence of the inaugural declaration of this term. We are willing to work together with all members. After the report, all Executive and Supervisory Committee members recited the oath. Then, Tao Baichuan, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered a training speech, and Wang Xiaolai of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce delivered a speech. Next, Xie Baochen of the Postal Administration, Jaffe Lin and Dai Baohua of the Shanghai Postal Administration, Ye Xianggao of the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, Lu Jingshi of the National Postal Workers' General Union, and guests such as Ren Jinping delivered speeches successively, with the speeches omitted for brevity.

Photo Session and Adjournment, Union Declaration 111

After the guests finished their speeches, Chairman Lu Keming delivered a closing speech. Everyone stood up and shouted slogans, then took a group photo and adjourned the meeting. After the meeting, representatives from all walks of life visited the union's office and club, where they were received by all members and treated with refreshments.

The declaration of the 11th Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union states: Time passes easily, and years flow like water. The 11th Executive and Supervisory Committees of this union now take office after the previous term. Reflecting on the past ten terms, their work has been gradual and meticulous. Whether for the country, society, the postal service, or postal workers, they have never considered themselves successful. However, the past achievements are undeniable. Therefore, looking back on the past and planning for the future, we hereby declare the future mission of this union on the day of our inauguration. Today, the country is in dire straits, and the world is changing rapidly. The country's hope is almost exhausted, and the country's peril and the shrinking of its territory should be deeply felt by all compatriots living today, and we should remember the danger while living in peace. Our postal workers have always taken serving the country and society as a prerequisite, and will continue to do so in the future. Feeling the current difficulties and deeply moved, we should be more encouraged to rise up and move forward bravely. Anything that benefits the country and society should be fought for together with our compatriots from all walks of life, and we will not hesitate to go through fire and water. This is the first point. The decline of the postal service in recent years has become an unprecedented phenomenon in the more than 30 years since the postal service was established. Our postal workers serve the postal service and are closely connected to it. How can we not feel sad when we see this situation? We have often studied the rights and wrongs, gains and losses, and the reasons for this situation. Although there are many reasons, the exhaustion of the postal service's economy and the decline of its business are the biggest fatal wounds. Therefore, today, to talk about the development of the postal service, the first thing is to stabilize the postal service's economy and restore its business. Our postal workers, as people who dedicate themselves to the postal service, sincerely hope to cooperate with the authorities with their love for the postal service. As for ourselves, we should work hard and impartially to improve work efficiency. This is the second point. Since its establishment, this union has experienced many difficulties. We deeply feel that the reason why this union has a long and glorious history today is due to the unity and support of all members on the one hand, and the completeness of the union's organization and the strictness of its discipline on the other hand. This enables all bad forces to have no opportunity to enter. Therefore, in order to maintain our hard-won union and its glorious history, we must strive for perfection and be more meticulous. We must not be satisfied with the past achievements, but take a step further to make this union militarized in terms of organization and discipline. In other words, all members, in addition to strictly abiding by the union's discipline, should absolutely obey the union's orders. In this way, the steps will be neat, the union's strength will be enriched, and the union's foundation will be more solid. This is the third point. The establishment of this union, internally, its greatest purpose is to gather the wisdom and strength of the masses to seek the welfare of the members, and to pay special attention to adapting to the needs of the members in all internal constructions. In recent years, the energy spent on this has been seen by all. Although it has experienced the changes of the January 28th Incident and was almost completely destroyed, the efforts of the previous Executive and Supervisory Committees and the supervision of all members have restored the inherent construction and improved it in a short time. From now on, we should follow this principle, not make empty words, pay attention to practice, and strive to achieve the realization of all constructions in the union. Moreover, we should organize a design committee to plan, weigh the urgency, and use a portion of the financial resources to run a portion of the business, so that all members can enjoy their due rights. This is the fourth point. Summarizing these four points is the entire mission of this union from now on. Based on the previous efforts, we will bury our heads in hard work and hereby declare this. Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, August 17, 1933.

Settlement of Seven Star Factory Closure Dispute 114

Both Parties Sign Three-Point Reconciliation Agreement

The Seven Star Copper Factory on Qimei Road, Hongkou, announced its closure due to operating losses and laid off more than 50 workers, causing a dispute. Yesterday, the Party and government jointly mediated, and the chairman persuaded the parties separately to reach a three-point reconciliation agreement: (1) The factory will subsidize worker Liu Guirong with 30 yuan. (2) The factory will introduce 28 jobs for workers Han Changfa and 56 others, and each of the remaining 29 workers will be given 5 yuan for travel expenses. (3) The wage issue of foreman Zhu Changgen will be resolved through legal proceedings due to a written dispute. Both labor and management expressed their agreement, and the reconciliation was concluded.

Page 13

Another Korean Youth Assassinated Yesterday After Yu Hui Guan's Death 115

The Deceased, Shi Xuanqiu, Had Just Moved from Hongkou to Shanzhong Road

Killed by a Korean in Fancy Clothes Yesterday Morning

丨Some Say It Was a Political Act, the French Police Are Taking It Very Seriously丨

Yesterday morning at around 6:00 a.m., a Korean youth was suddenly assassinated inside Lane 1270, No. 26, at the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Shanzhong Road in the French Concession. The assailant fired a total of three shots, all hitting the youth's vital parts, killing him on the spot. The details are recorded below.

Inside Korean Village 116

There are many Korean residents living in Lane 1270 near the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Shanzhong Road in the French Concession, which has become a special area for Korean residents, so the neighbors call it Korean Village. At the end of the lane is a one-story small western-style house, No. 26, whose landlord is also Korean, named Lin Haishan, a pen merchant, who lives upstairs. The downstairs living room is sublet to two Korean women, both of whom are young and attractive.

A Solitary Person 117

At the beginning of this month, Lin and his wife went to Beijing together, and their residence in Shanghai was entrusted to their relative Jin Ji to manage. At the same time, the remaining back room upstairs was sublet to a Korean youth named Shi Xuanqiu. Shi's original home was in Hamhung, Korea, and he is now 37 years old. He is a Korean ginseng merchant. He has only been in the house for a week. He has no family and few friends. He goes out early and returns late alone, which is his usual habit. He used to live in Hongkou for a long time, but for some reason, he recently moved to Avenue Joffre.

Violent Guest Opens Fire 118

At around 6:45 yesterday morning, after Shi got up, he was washing in the upstairs kitchen when a young man came, dressed in Chinese clothes and speaking Korean. When he saw Shi, he whispered to him. After Shi finished washing and went upstairs, the young man followed him. As soon as Shi entered the room, the young man took out a pistol from his sleeve and fired three shots at Shi. Shi fell to the ground in response, and the assailant turned around and escaped through the back door, disappearing in an instant.

Three Wounds 119

At that time, the cohabitants suddenly heard continuous gunshots upstairs and were all awakened, but to prevent accidents, they did not dare to open the door to check. After more than ten minutes, they opened the door to check and saw that Shi had fallen in a pool of blood. They touched him and found that he had already died. They reported it to the French police, and the police chief immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives to rush to the scene. After an inspection, they found that Shi had been shot three times, in the head, chest, and waist, and all of them were penetrating wounds.

Speculation on the Cause of Death 120

After the detectives finished their investigation, they collected three shell casings and the bullets that had penetrated the body and took them to the police station for investigation. Because the deceased was Korean, the police notified the Japanese consulate to send someone to the scene to take the body away for examination. However, according to general speculation, the reason for Shi's death was more likely a political act. However, the French Concession police authorities, seeing that Korean assassinations have occurred repeatedly recently, with the second one occurring just ten days after the recent killing of Yu Hui Guan, are taking it very seriously. It is said that they are planning to formulate measures to maintain order in the concession.

Yu Tianbi and Others Suggest That the Three Major Companies Open Special Departments for National Products 121

A Good Sign of the National Goods Year

Our country's production has declined, industry and commerce are sluggish, and people are accustomed to using foreign goods. To encourage the improvement of domestic goods and arouse the public's awareness, it is necessary to display, guide, and promote them. It is reported that Mr. Yu Tianbi, the former director of the Municipal National Goods Exhibition Hall, has seen this and suggested that the Nanjing Road Sincere, Wing On, and Sun Sun department stores open special departments for national goods to promote identification and encourage their use. The text of Mr. Yu's letter to the Shanghai Joint Association of Machine-Made National Goods Factories is recorded below. It begins: Today, all people of insight regard enriching national power and cultivating people's strength as the most urgent tasks. However, there is no other way to enrich and cultivate than to revitalize industry and promote national goods. Recently, various national goods manufacturers have been aware of this and have been able to work hard and devote themselves to saving the country in their respective positions. All of these situations can be said to be a good sign for the future of industry. However, when national goods are just budding, special attention should be paid to promotion to avoid stagnation. Although there are several national goods stores in this city, they are still too few considering the wide area of Shanghai, and their appeal is far less than that of the Sincere, Sun Sun, and Wing On department stores on Nanjing Road. Therefore, to achieve the smooth sale of national goods, it seems appropriate for manufacturers to jointly request that the department stores open special departments for national goods to achieve greater results. When Tianbi took office as the director of the Municipal National Goods Exhibition Hall last year, he had the intention to handle this matter. However, because his term of office was very short, he could not accomplish it. He then drafted a plan and suggested it to the Shanghai National Goods Promotion Association. Although it was reported in the newspapers and a reply was received that it had been adopted, it has not been implemented for many days, and this is a matter of concern. Therefore, based on his long-standing aspiration to serve society, he has raised the old matter again. He hopes that all national goods manufacturers will clearly understand the importance of joint sales and not be satisfied with the existence of several national goods stores, and will work together to achieve this goal. I hope you will consider my humble opinion. (The following is omitted.) The letter to the three major companies has the same general meaning and is omitted.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Anti-Theft Measures for Ocean Liners Are Strict 122

Iron Railings Installed, Firearms Added

Passengers Are Inspected Upon Boarding

There have been more cases of pirate attacks on ships this year than in any other year. After the Yu Shun incident of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the meeting on anti-theft on merchant ships convened by the Ministry of Communications agreed on measures that are being drafted and will be implemented soon. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's effective anti-theft measures began yesterday. The relevant information is reported below.

Ocean Liner Equipment Completed 123

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's anti-theft measures were already underway before the Yu Shun incident, including installing iron railings, isolating the watchtower, building a silver vault, acquiring more rifles and pistols, and adding a machine gun. In addition, more escort police teams were added to each ship, and the "Xin Ming," "Xin Feng," "Hai Yan," "Pu An," and "Tai Shun" ships were designated, costing a total of more than 30,000 yuan. Now, since the Yu Shun incident, the anti-theft work on each ocean liner has been carried out more actively. Except for the machine gun, which is still being applied for, the remaining arrangements have been completed successively. Passengers can now travel without worry.

Eight Russian Police Officers Assigned 124

There is a Russian police team of ten people in the bureau, originally prepared for temporary emergency needs and dispatched for escort. Recently, it has been noted that pirates are mixing in everywhere in Dapeng Bay, taking advantage of the opportunity to rob ships. Eight or nine out of ten of these pirates disguise themselves as passengers to board the ship and then rob it in the middle of the journey, which is really difficult to prevent. Recently, there have been frequent alarms in the Shanghai shipping industry. In order to prepare for unforeseen circumstances and prevent them in advance, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has added an inspection team starting yesterday, specializing in searching passengers on each ship to prevent pirates from mixing in. Eight Russian police officers have been assigned to be responsible for the inspection.

Inspection Began Yesterday 125

The Russian police's inspection of passengers began yesterday. It is temporarily limited to ocean liners. Regardless of whether it is the Tianjin, Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Ningbo, or Shantou, Guangdong, Hong Kong, and Xiamen liners, before the ship sails, when the passengers are all on board, the eight Russian police officers will board the ship with weapons. They will first search each passenger's luggage. Also, learning from the loss of the Yu Shun, the passengers' bodies will also be searched to prevent them from carrying weapons. First, second, and third class passengers must be searched, but special attention will be paid to steerage passengers. Yesterday, the Shanghai-Ningbo and Wenzhou liners were searched when they set sail. Even if there are pirates in the future, it will not be easy for them to mix in.

Plans to Follow Suit in Other Ports 126

The bureau also believes that when each ocean liner sails from various ports in the north and south oceans back to Shanghai, there are also passengers. If only export ships are searched, it is not a fundamental solution to prevent bandits. Therefore, it has been decided that each imported ship will also be searched. When ships depart from other ports, branch bureaus in each port will be telegraphed to implement searches for passengers disembarking at the local station, following the Shanghai bureau's methods. If any suspicious persons are found or weapons are confiscated, the passengers will be detained and handed over to the local military and police agencies for interrogation. As for the Yangtze River ships, because there are escorting soldiers, and river ships are not valued by bandits, because even if they rob, there is no place to escape, so each river ship will not be searched.

British Shipowner Dies Tragically 127

Stabbed to Death by a British-Russian Woman

The Da Mei Evening News reports that last night (16th) at around 11:00 p.m., Yang Si, a British shipowner, was seriously injured in a fight at his residence at No. 17, Lane 166, Maohai Road, and died in the ambulance on the way to the hospital. Yang's death is believed to have been caused by a fight with Mrs. Hartley, a British-Russian woman, who stabbed him with a knife. Mrs. Hartley was also stabbed in the chest, but the injury was minor. Yang was stabbed twice, and the wound on his right neck bled non-stop, leading to his death. Earlier, at around 10:10 p.m., the police received a phone call from his neighbor, reporting that he had seen the injured in a fight through the window. The police were dispatched, but no one answered the door. The police broke down the door and entered the room, and the police were almost tripped by Yang's body. Yang was lying in a pool of blood, and fresh blood was still gushing out from his neck. The police first tried to stop the bleeding and called an ambulance to take him to the General Hospital, but he died on the way due to excessive bleeding. The police later found Mrs. Hartley in the neighboring room, who was distraught and exhausted. It is believed that she was involved in the fight, and the wound on her chest was also bleeding non-stop. She was immediately taken to the General Hospital for treatment and then taken to the Tilanqiao police station for questioning. However, because she was mentally disturbed, the police could not find out what happened that night. According to what was heard this morning (17th), it is only known that she is a widow, 36 years old, and obtained British nationality in 1919. This morning at 11:30 a.m., the British police court sent someone to examine the body and then opened a court session at 2:30 p.m. After the judge read the charges, he said to the Russian woman, "I don't need to ask you whether you plead guilty or not, because I must send you to the Great Hall for trial." It is also heard that Yang had rented the house not long ago and bought a lot of furniture this week, which shows that he did not expect the danger of death to come before it happened.

Court Had Not Yet Approved Arrest Warrant, Lawyer Had Already Published Announcement 128

丨Containing the Phrase "Approved by the Court for Arrest"丨

Lawyer Yuan Xilian and Lin Zhongwen Are Jointly Sued

Chen Kan Accuses the Two of Joint Defamation and Claims Damages

Lawyer Yuan Xilian, as the representative of Lin Zhongwen, filed a case against Chen Kan, a Fujianese, in the Second Special District Local Court. Chen repeatedly failed to appear in court despite being summoned. Subsequently, Lawyer Yuan, on behalf of his client, published an arrest warrant in the newspaper. The arrest warrant contained the phrase "Approved by the Court for Arrest." Chen Kan read it and investigated with the Second Special Court. He found that at the time the advertisement was published, the court had not yet approved the application, and it was actually Yuan and Lin Zhongwen who fabricated the statement and published it in the newspaper. Therefore, he hired a lawyer to sue Yuan and Lin in the First Special District Local Court, requesting that the defendants be convicted of joint defamation and be ordered to compensate for reputational damages of 14,000 yuan. The First Special Court has repeatedly opened court to hear the case, as reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xue continued to hear the case. Only the defendant Yuan Xilian appeared in court. First, the plaintiff Chen Kan stated the reasons for the lawsuit in his Fujianese accent. Most of what he said was legal provisions and old and new precedents. He read aloud from the paper for a minute before stopping. Then, Yuan Xilian recounted the circumstances of handling the case, saying that Lin Zhongwen asked me to request an arrest in court on December 30 because Chen Kan had failed to appear in court twice. The judge verbally agreed that day. The next day, Lin came to inquire, and I told him that I had obtained permission. Lin then sent Chen's photo to the office. I then submitted a document with the photo to the Second Special District Local Court on January 4. On January 10, the case was again heard by the Second Special Court, and I again requested an arrest. The judge nodded again. The next day, Lin ordered his son to send the draft arrest warrant to the office. Because I had not yet seen the court's clear approval of the previous request for an arrest warrant, I instructed him to postpone the publication or change it to a warning. I stamped the draft and handed it back to his son, but I told him that if he wanted to publish this draft, he should wait for my notification. Unexpectedly, the newspaper had already been published on January 15, and I had no right to stop it. In short, lawyers handle cases with the client's intentions as their own, and all actions are naturally the responsibility of the client. However, the plaintiff is demanding that I compensate for damages of 14,000 yuan. I have no feud with Chen. It is purely that young people are being meddlesome and trying to show off, and so on. The court believed that the content of the case was already clear and did not need to be stated further. It ordered the lawyers of both parties to begin the final arguments and adjourned the court, announcing that the verdict would be announced on the 21st of this month.

Trial Opens for Wang Xiaomei's Lawsuit Against Zhang Shuliang for Sending a Small Coffin 129

Zhang Shuliang Has a Gold Tooth on His Upper Jaw

Coffin Shop Apprentice Identifies Him in Court

Trial Postponed to the 24th of This Month

Wang Xiaomei, a 19-year-old dance hostess at the Greater Shanghai Ballroom, resides at No. 6, Siming Lane, Xiafei Road. Recently, some dance patrons dissatisfied with her have often resorted to mischievous means, such as sending lavish meals for no reason or unexpectedly ordering a relocation truck to move her things. On the 23rd of last month, Wang was driving around when Car No. 92 followed her. On Yu Garden Road, it rammed into her bumper. Although there was no damage, it already broke her heart. Although Wang encountered the aforementioned incidents, she still tolerated it and kept silent. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 26th of last month at 11 o'clock, someone suddenly sent a small coffin to her home. According to national customs, a coffin entering the door is a sign of major misfortune. At this point, Wang Xiaomei could no longer bear it and immediately reported it to the police. At the time, there was no way to find the instigator, so they had to withdraw. However, when they questioned the apprentice who delivered it, named Zhang Guisheng, he said that if he encountered this person again, he would still be able to recognize him. Later, Wang Xiaomei thought carefully about the pranksters and concluded that they must be dance patrons who were dissatisfied with her. Therefore, during the tea dance at the Greater Shanghai Ballroom on the 30th of last month, she and Zhang Guisheng identified Zhang Shuliang, a native of Suzhou, 30 years old, and an employee of Jardine Matheson, among the dance patrons. As soon as Zhang Guisheng saw him, he identified him as the person who bought the coffin that day. However, Zhang Shuliang stated that this was not the case. As a result of the dispute between the two parties, they ended up at the Xinzha Police Station. After the head of the station investigated, he ordered them to file a lawsuit with the court. Wang Xiaomei then hired lawyer Wu Peng and filed a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing Zhang of insult. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the trial. Judge Wu Xiangzu presided over the questioning in the First Criminal Court. Because the details of the dispute between the two parties had already been published in the newspaper yesterday, the audience was very crowded. According to Wang Xiaomei's testimony, on the evening of the 23rd of last month, when she was driving around, a Mr. Zhou, together with Zhang, drove Car No. 92 and followed her. On Yu Garden Road, they intentionally made things difficult for her by hitting her bumper with their car, but there was no damage. The reason was that Mr. Zhou had accumulated hatred with me. At 11 o'clock in the morning on the 26th, an old craftsman and an apprentice from a coffin shop delivered a small coffin, claiming that it was purchased by my family. Because the visitor intended to insult me, I reported it to the police. Later, when I questioned the apprentice, I learned that someone else had instructed him to deliver it and that he could remember his clothing and special features. Therefore, later at the ballroom, he pointed out Zhang Shuliang. However, I did not know Zhang before. Usually, Zhang and a Mr. Zhou came to the ballroom together. The reason was that Mr. Zhou did not buy a ticket and wanted to go out with me, but I refused, which led to a feud, and so on. Next, according to Zhang Shuliang's testimony, he did not know Wang Xiaomei before. As for the evening of the 23rd, I was already asleep at home and did not go out driving. As for the delivery of the coffin on the 26th, I was handling matters at work at the time and did not go out either, and so on. Then, according to the witness Zhang Guisheng's testimony, he is 16 years old and lives at No. 15, Dali, Kaizi Road. He is an apprentice at the Xuchangxing Coffin Shop. At around 10 o'clock on the 26th, two people came to buy a small coffin and contacted my supervisor. At the time, the asking price was 3 yuan and 2 jiao, but the two people bargained down to 2 yuan and 5 jiao and ordered it to be delivered to No. 6, Siming Lane. On the spot, they personally wrote the address on a cigarette pack with a pencil. Then I accompanied the old supervisor to deliver it. One of the two people was wearing a light blue long gown and had a gold tooth on his upper right jaw. At this point, Judge Wu immediately ordered Zhang Shuliang to write "No. 5634, Wang Chuli's Residence" and other numbers in court and ordered him to open his mouth to examine the position and number of gold teeth he had, which were the same as those described by Zhang Guisheng. Because this case still requires the testimony of witnesses, he immediately ordered a postponement until 2 PM on the 24th of this month for the continuation of the trial. The defendant, Zhang Shuliang, was released on bail pending appearance.

It will still be called the Yangshupu Police Station. The area under its jurisdiction is the area east of the left bank of the Yangshupu River. Residents who need to contact the police station for matters should go to the new address from September 1st. The telephone numbers are 15380 and 50743. Also, the Yangshupu Police Station is under the jurisdiction of Police District "D" (B District). The office of the officer in charge of the district is located in the Jushan Police Station. Employees of the Telecommunications Machinery Manufacturing Plant Petition Party and Government Organs 133

And Seek Assistance from Various Organizations

The Ministry of Communications' Telecommunications Machinery Manufacturing Plant is now under orders from the Ministry to cease operations and is limited to closing by the end of this month. All employees will be given one month's salary as severance pay. However, all the technicians of the plant, because they are worried about their livelihoods after the plant closes, specially sent representatives to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to petition yesterday morning, and issued a declaration, requesting assistance from all sectors.

Request for Assistance from All Sectors 134

Yesterday morning at 9 o'clock, the factory workers' representatives Shi Mingpan, Shi Longbao, Yan Zimu, Zhou Shunde, Shi Aquan, Gan Lin, Ye Junru, etc., went to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to petition. The authorities sent personnel to receive them. The representatives then went to the National Telecommunications Workers' Association to request assistance. Their letter to the various associations requesting assistance stated: We, the technicians of the Ministry of Communications' Telecommunications Machinery Manufacturing Plant in Zhoujiadu, Pudong, respectfully report that we have suddenly received an order from the Ministry to cease operations due to "incomplete content" and to be dismissed by August 31st, etc. We have checked that the technicians have all been approved by the Ministry of Communications and have guarantees. Even if a technician makes a mistake, there are disciplinary regulations in the rules, and they cannot be dismissed without reason. As for the "incomplete content," there are those responsible, so how can it be blamed on the technicians? Most of the technicians have been practicing in the factory since they were young and have more than ten years of qualifications. Moreover, the skills they have learned are specialized in manufacturing various telecommunications machinery and various batteries, etc. Once they lose their jobs, there is nowhere to seek a livelihood. Moreover, the Ministry of Communications abruptly dismisses technicians halfway without reason, which is not in accordance with the law or regulations. Moreover, is the government currently providing relief to the unemployed? We have always admired your association's leadership of the people and engagement in construction. The technicians boldly submit this letter, earnestly requesting that you uphold justice and provide assistance.

Declaration of All Technicians 135

The factory workers issued a declaration stating: To the national telecommunications bureaus, telegraph bureaus, telephone bureaus, telecommunications organs, operators, technicians, mechanics, and various party and government organs, various labor unions, and various newspapers: We respectfully report that Director Yu Ruxin has recently issued a notice stating that according to the instructions of the Ministry of Communications, the content of this factory is "incomplete" and should be closed down immediately, completed within this month, in order to plan for improvement. All employees, except for telecommunications technicians and operators who should be transferred after the completion of the closure, should be dismissed and given one month's salary as severance pay, etc. This is a bolt from the blue, causing great consternation. We technicians are merely craftsmen and only know how to work on orders. If our skills are not good and we spoil the goods, causing losses to the factory, or if we intentionally sabotage or disobey orders, causing the director to be unable to exercise his duties, the director must distinguish between principals and accomplices and punish them accordingly. The four words "incomplete content" should not be applied to the technicians, causing us one hundred and several dozen technicians to lose our jobs and become beggars. But each person has a family, and one person's unemployment affects the whole family. In total, the lives of one thousand and several hundred people are at stake. Moreover, the responsibility for poor management lies with the director and has nothing to do with the technicians. How can the technicians be made to take responsibility for it, while the directly responsible director can take measures at his leisure, allowing the technicians to be slaughtered one by one? Moreover, most of the technicians have learned their skills in this factory and only know how to manufacture products for telegraph and telecommunications bureaus. They cannot undertake other work. In the Ministry of Communications, it is a specialized skill, and in society, it is discarded material. Apart from this, there is only a dead end. Just as operators only know how to send and receive telegrams and cannot take on other tasks, the Ministry of Communications has established operator regulations for the sake of protecting specialized skills, and they cannot be dismissed unless they violate the regulations. For us technicians, there are also special technician regulations. Now that the regulations have not been abolished, the technicians only know how to abide by the law. We especially request that all sectors uphold justice and provide assistance, and that the Ministry of Communications send personnel to rectify and resume work quickly, in order to maintain livelihoods and emphasize telecommunications. The technicians will certainly obey orders and follow instructions. We urgently submit this statement and await instructions with the utmost gratitude. Sincerely, all the technicians of the Ministry of Communications' Telecommunications Machinery Manufacturing Plant in Shanghai.

Soy Sauce Extract Contains Arsenic Poison 136

Ministry of Finance Advises Municipal Government to Investigate and Ban

The Ministry of Finance, according to the report from the Songjiang Salt Transport Deputy Envoy, stated that privately manufactured soy sauce extract in the Chinese areas and concessions of Shanghai hinders hygiene and affects tax sales. It has ordered the bureaus and districts to investigate and seize them, and requested that it be forwarded to the Municipal Government for investigation and ban, along with a list of factory addresses. The Ministry believes that this soy sauce extract is not manufactured like the soy sauce sold by soy sauce shops, which uses official salt. According to the Deputy Envoy's investigation, it contains arsenic poison. If this is true, it not only violates the salt regulations, but also endangers public health. Yesterday, it especially advised the Municipal Government to send letters to the concession authorities and instruct its subordinate bureaus to investigate and ban it, in order to emphasize hygiene and maintain the salt law.

Representatives of the China Walking Corps Arrive in Shanghai 137

The China Walking Corps is organized by more than a dozen young people with ambition in Guangdong. They plan to walk across the country for ten years to investigate the living conditions of people in various parts of the country and the reform of social undertakings. They have been approved by the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, and the General Headquarters of the China Boy Scouts to issue travel permits. They departed from Guangdong in 1931 and have been walking for more than two years, covering a distance of more than 27,000 li. Their footprints have spread throughout the provinces of Fujian, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Guangxi, Sichuan, and other provinces. After the corps arrived in Sichuan, it was divided into the Kangzang Team and the Mongolian-Hui Team. The Kangzang Team has now reached western Xikang and is temporarily staying in Ba'an for investigation due to a shortage of travel expenses. The Mongolian-Hui Team circled from Sichuan through Qin and Jin to Hebei Province and is expected to leave the Great Wall soon, passing through Suiyuan, Ningxia, Gansu, Qinghai, Xinjiang, and joining the Kangzang Team, then going to Inner and Outer Mongolia and the northeastern provinces, and returning to the central provinces. The corps has exhausted its funds due to long journeys and has been robbed by bandits eight times, losing almost all of its luggage. The journey ahead is long and expensive, and it is deeply feared that economic difficulties will hinder progress. It has specially sent Dong Shuhua, the director of the Mongolian-Hui Team, and Liu Huifang, a member of the corps, to Shanghai yesterday morning, intending to request assistance from the government and enthusiastic people in society and to purchase supplies, so as to complete this great feat as soon as possible. Currently, Mr. Dong and others are staying at the Hongkou Grand Hotel and will stay in Shanghai for three days before returning to Zhangjiakou.

Now it is known that

After district member Wang sent police to search in the nearby Huangpu River, Zhao's body was suddenly found at 5 AM yesterday on the surface of the river at the Youlong Wharf in the south. The uniform he was wearing was intact, but the waistband of his pants had fallen below his buttocks, and he seemed to have slipped and drowned in the river while defecating on the floating bridge of the wharf. The deceased has a wife and a son and a daughter at home, the son is 5 years old and the daughter is 2 years old, living together across from the Jiangbei Opera House in Yangjiadu. It is said that Zhao was very conscientious in his service.

Whose Property Is It?

Stevedore Attacked by Enemies 145

Li Tian, a Cantonese man, 29 years old, lives in the Waiyuan area of the Taikoo Wharf in Pudong and works at the Hongshun Mutual Aid Association in Yongxiang Lane, Hanbury Road, Hongkou, specializing in protecting goods on the Taikoo Wharf to prevent theft by petty thieves, which caused resentment among those people. Recently, Li suffered from illness and went to the Blue Cross Society across from Tianji Lane in Zhabei for treatment. He only recovered after a few days. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, he had just left the hospital and intended to go to the Hongkou Mutual Aid Association to discuss business. When he arrived at the intersection of West Wuchang Road and Tiemalu Road, he suddenly encountered four or five bums from the wharf. Seeing Li arrive, it was a narrow road for enemies. They raised their axes and slashed him four times, once on the right waist and three times on the right leg. He was seriously injured and bleeding profusely. The murderers, seeing that their purpose had been achieved, scattered like birds and beasts. After the attack, he was sent to the Tongren Hospital for treatment by patrol car.

Brotherly Quarrel; Sister-in-Law Grabs Knife to Join the Fray 146

Wounds Younger Brother's Right Hand

Xu Qian, a local old woman, 67 years old, lives in a bungalow at the intersection of Qiwupu Road and Huade Road in Yangshupu. She has two sons, the elder named Danan, 44 years old, who works as a farmer, and his wife Xia, who is about the same age. The younger son is named Xiaodi, 26 years old, who works as an electrician and has one wife and one concubine. Yesterday, Xiaodi was celebrating the festival at home and invited relatives and friends to gather together. At about 4 PM yesterday afternoon, Danan had an argument with Xiaodi over household matters, which escalated into violence. At this time, Xia, seeing that her husband Danan was outmatched, grabbed a kitchen knife and joined the fray, cutting her uncle Xiaodi's right hand, causing blood to gush out like a spring. He was later sent to the Tongren Hospital for treatment by ambulance.

Thugs at Taikoo Wharf Attack People with Knives 147

Two People Injured in the Attack; One Person Arrested on the Spot

At about 8 AM yesterday morning, in the shed in front of the patrolman's office at the Taikoo No. 2 Wharf on Xinkaihe Road, Jia Liang of the Fruit Guild was issuing tickets. Li Dexing and Chai Aru, sent by the Yongdalongmao Fruit Firm, were waiting to pick up goods at the wharf, waiting to receive tickets in order to pick up goods. Suddenly, four or five people arrived, all wearing short clothes and short pants and acting barbarically. One of them jumped and sat on a bench, obstructing work. Jia Liang and others knew that these people were not kind and did not argue with them. Suddenly, another person took Jia Liang's seat, so Jia Liang politely asked him to leave for work reasons. If Yan not only ignored him, but also punched him. Li Dexing and Chai Aru, who were next to him, stepped forward to dissuade him, but were instead twisted and killed. Another person went outside and snatched a knife from a stall on the road and brought it inside, slashing Chai Aru hard in the back. Li Dexing was also slashed in the head. The two were seriously injured and bleeding profusely and fell to the ground. The thugs, seeing that they had caused trouble, fled one after another. Later, the inspectors and patrolmen of the wharf arrived and sent the injured to the hospital for treatment, while pursuing the murderers. One person, named Li, a Cantonese, was arrested on the spot and sent to the Taikoo office. After questioning by a Westerner, he was immediately sent to the Daximen Bell Police Station for handling. It is heard that the murderer has been transferred from the Daximen Bell Police Station to the Lujiiawan Detention Center and will be sent to court for questioning this morning. Of the two injured, Li Dexing is not seriously injured, but Chai Aru's back is severely injured. According to the doctor, his life may be in danger.

Seize Life Steamer Smashes Child Trafficking Case 148

Huishan Police Station's Chinese Detective Wang Jinsheng, on the morning of the 6th of this month at 6:00 AM, apprehended four human traffickers: a woman named Xu He-shi, a woman named Yang Zhou-shi, Yang Pinming, and Jin Boxun, on board the Seize Life Steamer at the Jardine Matheson Wharf on Yuanfang Road. They rescued two children, an eight-year-old boy named Chen Genda and a five-year-old boy named Jinlong. The suspects were escorted to the First Special District Court for detention. Yesterday morning, the magistrate continued the interrogation. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated that during the adjournment, the families of the two children had not been located and requested further investigation. When questioned, Xu He-shi claimed that the child Genda was entrusted to her by his uncle, A'er, to bring to Shanghai. Yang Zhou-shi confessed to having cohabited with Yang Pinming for many years. Because they had no children, they spent sixty yuan to buy Jinlong as their son. Yang Pinming claimed that Jinlong was purchased from the Su countryside as a son. Jin Boxun confessed that a friend had asked him to send the child to the ship, which was true. The police lawyer stated that it was clear that the defendants intended to take the two children to Shantou for sale and should be severely punished. Magistrate Xiao ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody for sentencing at a later date.

Li Jiacang Commits Suicide Under an Assumed Name 149

Li Jiacang, a native of Yin County, Ningbo, was 26 years old and unmarried. He worked as a traveling salesman at the Nanchang Copper Factory at 820 North Zhejiang Road. He had no particular hobbies but enjoyed drinking. Recently, due to unknown reasons, he became depressed and unhappy and took his own life. He suddenly went out alone and did not return for two or three days. The factory sent people to search for him everywhere, but he was nowhere to be found. They sent a letter urging his brother, Li Xuqing, to come to Shanghai to help with the search. They searched all the hotels and hospitals but still found no trace of him. Unexpectedly, Li, on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at 5:00 PM, checked into the Taihua Hotel on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession under the assumed name of Li Junhua, a local resident, renting a small room. He committed suicide by taking poison that night. It was not until 10:00 AM yesterday that the tea boy, Qian Rongqing, discovered him. He had already died. The police were immediately notified and sent detectives to take the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for an autopsy. A membership card of the Ningbo Fellow-Townsmen Association was found on his person. After inquiries with the association, his real name and business address were obtained. His brother was notified and went to the funeral home to identify the body. It was confirmed to be him. A report will be submitted to the Second Special District Court today for an investigation.

Trial of the "Little Bullhide" Appeal Case 150

Cao Chenglin, a gangster in Hongkou nicknamed "Little Bullhide," was shot and killed by his enemies on the evening of May 15th last year at 11:00 PM at the intersection of West Xinqiao Street and Caishi Street in the French Concession. The murderer fled. It was not until May of this year, almost a year later, that the French police detective arrested a suspect named Wang Caibao in Taiyuan Fang on Caishi Street and sent him to the Second Special Court. He was charged with premeditated murder. Wang was found guilty and sentenced to life imprisonment. Wang, dissatisfied with the verdict, filed an appeal with the Third Branch of the High Court. Based on the appeal, the High Court summoned police detective Zhou Yaoting and detectives Zhang Chunsheng and Wang Licheng to the court yesterday morning. Judge Fan Peien brought the appellant Wang Caibao to court for questioning in the Fifth Tribunal. Wang denied being an accessory to the murder, completely overturning his original testimony and vehemently claiming his innocence. As a result of the court discussion, the appellant was remanded in custody, and the hearing will be adjourned for further evidence.

Novel Lanterns and Art Performance

All kinds of arrangements are extremely perfect

Shanghai Chuyi Company, in order to revitalize the market in South Shanghai and promote noble entertainment, has scheduled a day and night amusement fair at Bansongyuan in South Shanghai starting on the 25th of this month. Educational News

Important News: Ministry of Education Explains the Education Association Law 165

With Special Circumstances Exception

According to the Fujian Provincial Department of Education, Article 6 of the Education Association Law stipulates that the area of an education association shall be based on the existing administrative area, but this shall not apply if there are special circumstances in the district education association that have been approved by the supervisory authority. The Department of Education has issued instructions that the so-called special circumstances should be interpreted in accordance with the law and that the regulations are not explicitly stipulated. The instructions of the Ministry of Education state that the above-mentioned facts need to be examined in detail. The special circumstances referred to in the proviso to Article 6 of the Education Association Law must have obvious facts and sufficient reasons to prove that the district education association needs to have an area that does not conform to the existing administrative area to conform to the meaning of the four characters "special circumstances". For example, if the number of members in an administrative area is less than 20, or if administrative area A is too vast compared to administrative areas B and C, and education is particularly developed, etc.

Single Overseas Study Regulations of Provinces and Cities Should Be Revised 166

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities, requiring that the single overseas study regulations of all provinces and cities should be revised in accordance with the regulations for studying abroad, and submitted for approval within one month after receipt of the document.

Local

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Prohibition of Dual-Class System in Middle Schools 167

The Municipal Education Bureau of this city, believing that some private middle schools in this city have adopted a dual-class system, which has led to abuses, instructed various middle schools yesterday to pay attention to correction. The original order stated: "The adoption of a dual-class system in primary schools is a last resort. The content of the middle school curriculum is complex, and guidance takes time. This type of system is not applicable. However, in recent years, private middle schools in this city have often adopted this type of system, only seeking to save school expenses, without considering the interests of students, which is extremely inappropriate. Recently, the Ministry of Education promulgated Article 21 of the Middle School Regulations, which states that 'All subjects in middle school, except physical education and military training, may adopt other grouping methods for teaching, but may not be taught in combined classes'. According to this regulation, all subjects in middle school should be taught in separate classes to emphasize academics and comply with the decree. From the 22nd year of the Republic of China, all private middle schools in this city must not adopt a dual-class system for teaching, so as to emphasize academics and comply with the decree."

The original letter is as follows: Respectfully, as the brutal Japanese ravage our land and the nation faces peril, the idea of saving the country through aviation is shared by all. Since your association initiated the fundraising for aviation donations, all the university students in Shanghai have taken the lead as young pioneers, either enthusiastically donating or actively fundraising, amounting to a considerable sum, which can be easily verified. This semester, to further enhance the effectiveness of fundraising, we have jointly organized a committee across various schools to raise funds for a "Shanghai University Students Aircraft," planning steps and actively proceeding. Now, to promote the success of donations and encourage patriotic spirit, we propose that one of the aircraft purchased and arriving soon be designated as the "Shanghai University Students Aircraft." We would appreciate your response on this matter.

President of Shanghai College of Law and Politics Submits Petition to the Ministry of Education Requesting Approval to Rescind Order to Cease Enrollment 172

The Shanghai College of Law and Politics received an order from the Ministry of Education in July of this year to cease enrollment. The acting president of the college, Zhang Zhongdao, traveled to Beijing to personally meet with Minister Wang, presenting the difficulties faced. He also submitted a separate petition to the Ministry of Education requesting approval to rescind the order to cease enrollment. The submitted document is recorded below: Petition to clarify difficult circumstances, humbly requesting review and approval to rescind the order to uphold education and facilitate rectification. Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's instruction No. 9616, which forwarded the Ministry's instruction No. 7020, ordering the college to cease enrolling new students and transfer students, to provide an opportunity for final rectification, etc. Upon receiving this, the college felt nothing but dismay. The Ministry's rectification of education naturally has its own standards, which the college need not reiterate. However, we believe that education is a grand plan for cultivating talent, and to achieve good education, it cannot be accomplished overnight. It requires time to allow for thorough implementation, so that progress can be made gradually and perfection can be approached step by step. Even among the current national universities, there are still areas that do not fully meet expectations, let alone private universities, whose finances rely solely on private individuals and whose measures often face obstacles. This situation is well known to experienced educators like yourselves. The college, mindful of its past history and future mission, has been diligently determined to implement the improvements outlined in the Ministry's instruction No. 1853 issued in March of this year. We have already reported on the progress and plans for improvement in April of this year, submitting them for your review and guidance. Among these, regarding academic matters such as student level, faculty compensation, curriculum arrangement, etc., and regarding general affairs such as equipment, campus, funding, etc., aside from a small portion that can be improved as much as possible in the shortest amount of time, other aspects such as raising student levels and faculty compensation, constructing campuses, and raising funds cannot be expected to be achieved in three months. However, for the sake of future development, the college has been constantly deliberating and striving for results in the three months following the order to implement improvements, hoping to live up to the Ministry's intentions of supervision. We have drafted a plan to implement strict entrance exams for new students starting in the 22nd academic year, and to provide rigorous training for both new and old students alike. In addition to finding ways to raise faculty compensation, we are also proceeding with the construction of a new campus. On July 9th of this year, the board of directors held a meeting, attended by nine directors including Mr. Li Shizeng, Mr. Du Yuesheng, and Mr. Wei Daoming. It was resolved to commence construction on the approximately 90-acre campus site purchased by the college in Beiqiao Town at the beginning of the academic year, proceeding step by step with all our efforts. We believe that our dedication will be understood by all, and that even if we cannot receive support from the authorities, we will not suffer unexpected destruction. The college originally scheduled the enrollment advertisement for July 5th and 6th as the examination dates. Later, according to the Ministry's instruction No. 5948, the enrollment dates had to be changed to late July at the earliest. The college complied with the order, changed the dates, published the correction, and reported it for record. The college has always respectfully and diligently followed the Ministry's orders without any negligence. We sincerely did not expect to be subject to the penalty of ceasing enrollment just after the first enrollment examination was completed. Preventing the college from continuing enrollment is tantamount to interrupting its life. Therefore, we dare to present the difficulties and circumstances to Your Excellency. We believe that an independent college is different from a comprehensive university. If one department of a university ceases enrollment, there are other departments to sustain it. This is not the case for an independent college. If one department ceases enrollment, then all first-year students in all departments will inevitably be completely suspended and unable to attend classes. This not only makes the curriculum arrangement incomplete, but also makes it impossible to connect the courses taught. This is the first difficulty. Since private schools do not have state funds to rely on, their financial resources depend heavily on student tuition and fees for maintenance. The college enrolled nearly 300 students last year. If enrollment is stopped, revenue will be sharply reduced by more than 30,000 yuan, which will inevitably have a significant impact on administrative expenses. This is the second difficulty. Since private school tuition is higher than that of any national school, the only way to attract students is through the school's reputation. Once enrollment is stopped, the school's reputation will suffer a great loss. Students in other grades will also seek to transfer to other schools. In this case, the number of students in the current year will not increase and may even decrease. How can the future be sustained? This is the third difficulty. The college's various plans for vigorous improvement have already been described above. If the above three difficulties are suddenly added to impede and obstruct the college, it may discourage those who are running the school and hinder the college's path to active improvement. We believe that the Ministry's repeated orders for improvement are intended to urge improvement, without any other intention. The Ministry should also uphold the spirit of impartiality and altruism to help those who are extremely willing to be responsible for improvement but face various difficulties, so that they can gradually flourish and develop, and truly have the opportunity to achieve final rectification. All the reasons for clarifying the difficult circumstances are presented in this document for your examination and verification. We request that you promptly rescind the order and temporarily allow the college to continue enrolling students, while ordering a deadline for improvement. The college will be very fortunate, and education will be very fortunate. Respectfully submitted.

Wimbledon World Tennis Championships Diary (II) 179

Special Correspondence from London by Yizhi Ji

June 29th (Thursday)

Today was a quiet day, with no startling events or surprises, but there were many matches worth noting. Some matches even required watching until 8:00 PM when the lights came on. The sunlight was thin, the temperature was pleasant, and the courts were full of spectators. The outer courts were crowded, making it impossible for those who were not close to see. The ball boys were poorly trained, even on the center court. They often held the ball for a long time and did not know how to throw it, or let it roll around on the court during the match. One boy even caught a ball that was in play, even though it was sure to go out of bounds.

Seed and Cramm occupied the honored center court, with Vines and Miki in the first match. Seed won with three straight sets. The first set was won easily, the second set was much more difficult, and there was some concern for him during the third set. Seed's shots were full of judgment, and his net play was consistent with his planned strategy. His forehand and backhand shots were exceptionally even and very accurate, with few errors. His serve was also better than usual, and he constantly rushed to the net, usually successfully. He was often troubled by high balls, but he always smashed them with powerful or sharp-angled shots. Cramm's balls mostly came from the back court, and his groundstrokes were very good, but he made too many errors. He almost never came to the net, indicating his ability to defend on the baseline. In the first set, his defense was tight, making it very difficult for Seed to break through. The third set was a test for Seed. When Cramm was leading five to three, he had three chances to win the set with one shot, but Seed broke through and tied it at five to five. When leading eight to seven, Cramm served an unreturnable heavy ball, but it was ruled a foot fault. In any case, Seed had enough to benefit from it.

Faucquier had beaten Punnett, but in the first match, he lost to Menzel in three straight sets. This Czech player's shots were as hard and aggressive as this South African's, but he was more careful and attentive. The white lines of the court were his target, and although some of his shots were just barely out, most of his shots were unreturnable. Although Menzel was a large and fat man, he was dangerous and had to be constantly attacked.

Austin and Gran Hill competed on the center court, and Austin's victory was assured and well-deserved. His performance was straightforward and flawless, with nothing to fault. His serve was the best ever seen from his racket. Unfortunately, his right foot always swung over the line with each shot. The referee, who was supposed to pay special attention to foot faults, was deaf and dumb. Austin's footwork and angled shots were excellent, and whether he was backcourt stroking, net volleying, or hitting high or low balls, he was equally powerful.

Only in the second set did Gran Hill fight bravely, tying it at five to five. His serve was broken three times, making it equal, but his own serve was ineffective, and he ended the second set with a score of ten to eight. Austin broke his serve in style and got it again. The third set was one-sided, and Gran only won one game.

This second set, with its even battle formation, was the only good match seen on the center court. When Gran Hill recovers his form, he will be able to defeat the best or near-best Austin. Although Austin maintained his high position, he was often stumped by Gran, causing him to hesitate and make many errors. Gran Hill had a line ball that Austin let go, but it turned out to be a good ball that touched the line. Austin raised both hands to indicate his mistake. When he missed a kill shot, he couldn't help but sigh. In this critical situation, Austin's performance was not like that of an Englishman at all. The audience did not pay attention to this, but only enjoyed the excellence of his performance.

The ambitious Stephanie easily defeated Merlin, while Poullain swept Tunbel after a hard-fought set, six to zero, six to one. Spencer's victory over Crape was a surprise. These two South Africans only decided the winner after five sets. Crape, who held the racket with his left hand, was leading two to one, and his victory seemed certain, but he suddenly slumped and lost two sets in a row. Crape's serve was terrifying, aggressive, and swift. Spencer's return was excellent, never loosening up in the slightest.

On the center court, Sato and Bouin performed beautiful tennis skills, defeating Mann and Kellen in three straight sets. Their perfect cooperation was admirable. Mann and Kellen had mutual flaws and made no progress.

The women's doubles match on the center court started at nearly 7:00 PM, and the audience stayed without leaving. Miss Rounde and Miss Sheeran faced Miss Jie Gu Bai and Mrs. King (formerly Miss Ford). Jie Jin won the first set, but lost the rest. The decisive set was tied at six to seven games. Rounde finally advanced and won.

The cooperation between Miss Jie Gu Bai and Mrs. King is especially unique in women's doubles. One defends the net, and the other defends the baseline. The baseline long strokes are numerous and delayed, becoming monotonous, but their tactics are particularly beautiful and still make the audience happy and surprised. The ball flies back and forth from both corners, and the net defender waits for the opportunity to catch and kill. Miss Rounde is better, while Jie Gu Bai showed instability after the first set. Many good and easy opportunities were missed. Miss Sheeran is slightly better than Mrs. King. Both are good at running and do not know fatigue.

The match between Mrs. Maddy and Miss Sheeran made the court more colorful. Sheeran wore a backless top with two crisscrossing straps, while Mrs. Maddy often stayed on the baseline to stroke. The opponent was the first-ranked player in England, so the match lasted a long time. Mrs. Maddy made more mistakes than expected, but she still won the match, only losing three games. Miss Skrivan faced Miss Lierre, and Lierre resisted for a long time, winning the first set and almost winning the third. This match was held on the sixteenth court, and the audience was crowded, with no room to move. Miss Lierre's performance was excellent, and those who did not see it were bound to feel sorry.
