Spring and Autumn

Summoning-Rent Literature 185

— Shen Yan

Ten odd years ago, when I first came to Shanghai, the first thing that caught my attention was the many small red paper slips plastered at the entrances of various alleyways and on various utility poles. With my limited knowledge, I always thought they were Fu (fortune) or Shou (longevity) characters, or signs indicating auspicious directions. Later, I made a point of taking a closer look and found that they were advertisements for vacant houses for rent, with the heading "Summoning Rent." "Summoning Rent" is originally a short idiom, but Shanghainese use it as a noun. Thus, summoning rent became a thing. If you ask someone, "Has the summoning-rent paper been posted?" people will laugh at you, because the usual way to say it is, "Has the summoning rent been posted?" Therefore, the "summoning rent" I am talking about here is also a thing, not an idiom.

Since there are so many "summoning rents" posted everywhere in Shanghai, and as soon as one is torn down, another one immediately takes its place, then all Shanghainese, all literate Shanghainese, must be good at writing "summoning rents." That's what I always thought at first. At the same time, I also felt that the language on these "summoning rents," if extrapolated using the principle of "practice makes perfect," would definitely be outstanding and surprising. Therefore, I paid attention to appreciating them at all times. The result, however, was extremely disappointing. Often, out of ten "summoning rents," their language, such as "water and electricity included," "living room shared," etc., nine of them are exactly the same. And at the end, they always have to add that nonsensical phrase "No families, please."

Once, it was my friend Dr. X's turn to write a "summoning rent." Unexpectedly, when the old man picked up the pen, he also wrote a long, stereotypical passage as usual. Finally, he also smoothly wrote the character "No"... At this point, I couldn't bear it any longer and immediately stood up to stop him. "It's rare that you're also writing 'summoning rents'! Why don't we take this opportunity to talk about 'summoning-rent literature'?" I suggested to him with great excitement.

"Good! Then please express your opinion first!"

"I think other things can be temporarily ignored, but the phrase 'No families, please' must be immediately eliminated with revolutionary means. Because based on the literal meaning, this sentence only has two explanations:

(1) Those who do not have kinship with the landlord should not ask.

(2) Men and women who are not formal family members should not ask.

However, the original intention of the person writing the "summoning rent" is definitely not the above two points, but rather "no renting to those without families," and they would also never investigate whether the woman you bring is your formal family member. As long as you are not a bachelor, you can definitely ask about it. So, the word "No" obviously has no possibility of existing and should be replaced with the word "Without"!"

After listening, Dr. X repeatedly agreed, but then picked out a newspaper from a pile of them. "Simply changing one character doesn't count as a revolution in 'summoning-rent literature.' Look at the title of this section of 'summoning rent.' Isn't it fresh and lively!"

I took the newspaper and looked at it. It turned out to be the six characters "Attention, Child Lovers." It was indeed a very eye-catching title. Who would have thought that below it was an advertisement for a house for rent near a French park?

I immediately expressed my deep admiration for the author's ingenuity and even asked Dr. X to let me cut out this section of the "summoning rent" to preserve it. From then on, everyone knew that I especially liked to study "summoning-rent literature." Soon, a friend who lived at the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Rue Luban in the French Concession came to me, asking me to draft a "summoning rent" for him. I thought for a long time and fortunately did not submit a blank paper. The topic was "Prerequisites for Choosing a Residence." In addition to the usual stereotypical phrases such as "spacious house, ample light," I also added the sentence, "Ideally located at the intersection of various tram lines in the French Concession." My friend left very satisfied. Later, I learned that as soon as this "summoning rent" was posted, his house was rented out that very morning.

Between Husband and Wife 186

— Qian Yun

(1)

Once, when the doorbell rang, the wife intentionally faced the bed, pretending to be asleep, anticipating that he would definitely sit close to the bed, perhaps giving her a light, sneaky kiss. When the kiss landed, she unexpectedly grabbed his neck, which would be quite interesting. However, she later found out that it was a classmate who had come. The wife pouted, and the classmate thought he had offended her somewhere. He never understood the secret behind it. After the wife told her husband, she said:

"I'll tell him tomorrow."

The wife wrinkled her nose and laughed, saying:

"You dare?"

(2)

The wife often instructed the husband:

"Finish work early and come back sooner. You know, waiting makes people anxious!"

The husband felt very happy, but in the evening, he intentionally came home a little later than usual. As expected, he saw that his wife was very unhappy. The husband regretted it, thinking that it was extremely meaningless. While he was deliberately prolonging the time outside, he felt equally lonely. Therefore, he carefully said to his wife:

"I'm willing to accept your punishment."

The wife lay on the bed, so angry that she didn't move. He lifted her arm to look: It turned out that the wife was laughing. So, as if granted amnesty, he also laughed. But in the end, the wife solemnly said:

"Don't do it next time!"

(3)

The husband, due to several unfinished matters, could not go to his hometown with his wife. After the train left, the wife frowned from time to time and didn't even eat lunch. Many people in her hometown asked about him, and the wife felt that they respected him, which secretly pleased her. But as soon as she thought about him not being by her side, she felt that everything was uninteresting, and she was unhappy all day long! The next day, the wife couldn't bear the loneliness any longer and wrote him a letter, writing only one sentence:

"Qing: I'm really not happy!"

The husband was initially confused when he saw it. Later, after thinking about it, he finished his work and immediately started his journey. When they met, the wife was still like in the letter, simply saying:

"Tonight, I can sleep peacefully!"

The husband smiled, proudly embraced his wife, and was about to kiss her; but the sound of their mother's footsteps gradually approached.

Putting the Cart Before the Horse 187

— Si Su

Fish is what I desire, and bear's paw is also what I desire. If I cannot have both, I will give up fish and take bear's paw. There are many such things in the world! In the great fire in Caonitang, Laobaidu, Pudong, on the ninth day of the ninth lunar month, I heard about this kind of irreconcilable fact again. The result was also taking one thing that was desired and giving up another. But weighing the importance of the two is exactly the opposite of giving up fish and taking bear's paw. This shows that one side is wise, and the other is foolish.

When the great fire in Caonitang, Laobaidu, Pudong, had just been extinguished, I happened to have something to do in Pudong. I heard many rumors about the fire. The most tragic one was, of course, "eight or nine children were burned to death." At that time, someone explained the reason: the families of those who were burned were all boatmen or stevedores working at the docks. During the day, the men and women were not at home. All the children could not be taken with them, and if they were left at home, they could not guard the house. They had no choice but to lock the two doors, locking the children inside. As a result, when the fire broke out, the locked children could not escape and were burned to death. There was also a family where a five-year-old boy was already being carried in his mother's arms; in that glimpse, she suddenly remembered that there were twenty yuan on the bed. She hurriedly threw the child away and went in to get the money. Because the fire was getting fiercer, she only felt that escaping was important, and she forgot about the child. By the time she realized it, it was too late to go back in and save him! The next day, the rumor that eight or nine people were burned to death was confirmed to be a rumor. Only one person was burned to death, and he was indeed five years old, named Zhang Zhilong. Although it is not known whether he was harmed because his mother took twenty yuan, the victims were all very poor people, with most families having no food for the next day. However, the neck of the burned child's corpse had a silver necklace around it. This is somewhat similar to the twenty-yuan theory. If this taking and giving up is not a rumor at all, then the one who took and gave up was most likely Zhang Zhilong's mother.

Fish is originally not as good as bear's paw. One would only take fish if there was no bear's paw. With bear's paw, it becomes a treasure in front of one's eyes. Of course, one must give up fish and take bear's paw. Mencius was a wise man. How could he take the lesser of the two? A foolish woman is still a foolish woman. She only knows that money is precious. A five-year-old son is not as good as twenty yuan. She put the cart before the horse. However, looking around, it is not only foolish women who put the cart before the horse. Even some who consider themselves smart are still persistently confused about putting the cart before the horse!

Soliciting Submissions for Old He Yu's Sixty-Sixth Birthday Sentiments and Poetry Manuscripts 188

— Xuange

Jianghuai, ancient land of heroes, harboring the old man who startles spring; with three unrivaled talents, he spins silk, lamenting the difficulty of achieving peace. Climbing to heights, he still considers the small state of Lu, pondering on the water's journey. In the capital, dreams and memories merge, he's seen it all. Exhausting drafts, he writes of future paths. Returning, silks and treasures are sought at the edge of the sea. With a cane, he wanders past Ming Lake, chanting of willows. If poetic friends can be summoned, wait until next year when the crabapples bloom. (In his residence, there is a crabapple tree over a hundred years old.) Extending longevity, a drunken pact is made with Pearl Spring, to reflect our faces together in the waves.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 189

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirteen

Abandoning His Post to Meet a Soulmate, a Beauty Silently Permits

Inheriting a Family Fortune, a Strong Man Rejoices Wildly

When　Ms. Jiang saw this situation, it was clear that her daughter had completely agreed. Generally speaking, she had always been in favor of the Zhao family's marriage proposal, but her daughter had been picky. Now it was different, it had turned into her daughter being in favor and herself being picky, wasn't this a strange thing? Guan Yaowu's unfinished cigarette was still on the table, so Ms. Jiang picked one up and started smoking it herself, occasionally glancing at her daughter. Gui Zhi said: If you have something to say to me, just say it, why are you always spacing out? Ms. Jiang said: You agreed to this marriage with your own mouth, don't regret it later. Gui Zhi straightened her face and said: Regret what? I've seen through people's hearts. Men all treat women as toys, wanting them when they're happy, and not wanting them when they're not. I only know of men who lose women and then go find a job, but I've never heard of men who lose a job and then accommodate a woman. If you want to see people's hearts, you can see it from this. The world is just about exchanging hearts for hearts, I feel satisfied with this kind of thing. Jiang Dai quietly finished smoking that cigarette, nodded and said: As long as you say these words, what else can I say, then I'll just follow your wishes. Gui Zhi sat quietly on the side, without saying anything else. After a while, she heard the sound of leather shoes echoing out from the backyard, as if Company Commander Guan had left. Immediately afterward, Mr. Zhao in the backyard opened his throat and started singing opera there. Gui Zhi hadn't heard the sound of opera in the backyard for several days, the fact that the old gentleman was singing again at this time meant that the old gentleman was happy. In her heart, she thought about how the Zhao family could see her in a good light, unlike the Gan family, whose head of the bureau wanted to kick the poor children out. These past few days, the old gentleman probably knew that the marriage had changed a little, but when he met her, he still smiled, which was unlike that Master Gan, who would turn his back on people as soon as he changed his face. As she thought this way, she felt more and more the goodness of the Zhao father and son. (161)

Small Recipe

My Eating Experience 190

— Ke Ding'an

The　weather is so hot, everyone is clamoring, and in the steaming heat, the weak life is easily attacked by various microbes. A moment of carelessness can lead to illness, which is a very dangerous thing! The ancients said: "Illness enters through the mouth," which is absolutely correct. So how should we be careful in choosing food in this dangerous season? What I am talking about here is the vegetables I often eat, which I think are very hygienic.

Ice-Crystallized Snow Chicken: There is a stall in the small vegetable market that specializes in selling whitened chicken. You can buy it for six small ocean coins and enjoy this flavor. Method: First, wash the white chicken with water and put it in a small jar, add a little water. Then, use agar-agar (commonly known as vegetable gelatin, produced in Japan. Recently, we have good vegetable gelatin coming from Qingdao, the quality is very good), cut it finely and add it, boil it until the white chicken is suitable for your teeth to chew, sprinkle with salt, pour in rice wine, and add MSG and other seasonings. (Be sure not to use soy sauce.) When the taste has penetrated into the white chicken, take it out, let it cool, and put it in the refrigerator. After two hours, prepare a large basin, take out the white chicken, and turn it upside down in the basin. This icy and fresh snow chicken will be dancing on your tongue.

Red and White Intermingling: The middle waist peak of the best-quality Zhejiang Xue Tui ham is the best part of the ham. Clean the accumulated dirt on the outside, take out the fresh red meat, and carefully cut it into thin, short strips (about one and a half inches long). Separately, buy a piece of chicken breast meat, cook it, and tear it into thin shreds, preferably cut to the same length as the ham shreds. If you like the taste of ginger, you can also add some thin ginger shreds. Place the cut ham shreds in a bowl, seal it with cotton paper, steam it on top of the rice cooker, take it out and let it cool, mix in the ginger shreds, and mix with refined salt, MSG, and rice wine. It is very fresh and delicious to use as an accompaniment to wine. It is also refreshing and pleasant to use with rice.

Crepe-Like Pig Trotters: Some friends don't like to eat meat in summer, but this method of eating is the best. Method: Wash fresh pig trotters and boil them thoroughly in boiling water. Put them in a bamboo basket and drain the water. Separately, use an iron wok to boil raw oil or vegetable oil thoroughly, put the pig trotters in, and fry them as much as possible, making sure that the skin of the pig trotters forms a honeycomb shape and the lean meat is also about the same. Take it out, drain the oil, and soak it in cold water. When the skin of the pig trotters is soaked, put washed Chinese cabbage in the pot, add a little water, put the pig trotters on top, and add salt, wine, and soy sauce. (If you like the aroma, you can also add fennel, cinnamon, etc.) Cover the pot tightly, do not open it halfway. Simmer over low heat for an hour, then take it out of the pot. The aroma is excellent, unprecedented. As for the rich and delicious taste, it is even more indescribable. The Chinese cabbage at the bottom also has a special flavor.

Mustard Eel Slices: If it is only for two or three people to eat, then it is enough to buy four thick yellow eels. To eat this, the cruelty is real. Nail the head of the eel to a square board, and use a small knife to open it on its back (hold the tip of its tail with your left hand). It is best to only use the fat meat on its back. After opening it, cut it into one-and-a-half-inch-long slices, spread them on a bamboo basket and let them dry. Start another oil pan, pour it in and fry it thoroughly, add rice wine, refined salt, and then add the prepared mustard powder, stir evenly with a spatula. After all the water in the pot is absorbed into the eel slices, take it out. The clear and lasting taste can hang on your taste buds.

Spicy Ribs: Buy pre-cut ribs from the butcher shop, wash them, let them dry, and soak them in good light soy sauce. After the salty taste has penetrated, mix a little flour into the egg white, pour the ribs in and stir evenly. Boil raw oil or vegetable oil, put the ribs in one by one and fry them thoroughly. Take it out and drain the oil. Separately, mix chili powder and sesame oil evenly, put the ribs back into the pot, pour in the mixed chili powder, stir quickly with a spatula, and then take it out of the pot. In addition to the flavors of pepper salt, sugar, and vinegar, it will make you taste another kind of flavor.

Jadeite Topping: This is a common and flavorful dish. Use four green-shelled duck eggs, break them in a large bowl. Separately, use lean and fatty ham (i.e., half red, half white), cut into similarly narrow (about one and a half inches long, about three minutes wide) small pieces, spread around the bowl, red facing out, white facing in. Then, use a fresh lotus pod, peel off the hard skin of each seed tip, then cover the bowl with another bowl in the center of the egg (to prevent water vapor from entering). Steam it on top of the rice cooker. When eating, you will feel a clear fragrance, very much like "this dish should only be found in heaven."

Page 17

Free Talk

Let the Womenfolk Have a Go! 191

— Lin Yutang

Last week I saw a news item in the mainland newspapers. An American woman, the president of some Women's Rights League, named something like Mrs. Inez Hayne, I can't quite remember. She said, as if divinely inspired, that the world ruled by men had become a mess. From now on, women should be allowed to try ruling the world, and then there would be a solution.

As one of the men who "rule the world," I am in complete agreement with this proposal. I never wanted to rule the world in the first place. After ruling for half my life, I'm a little tired of it, and I'm willing to abdicate and hand over the world to any fool brave enough to take on this responsibility. I'd like to take some time off. I'm a thorough failure. I think all honest men will agree with me. Even if the aborigines of Tasmania were willing to come forward and take on this responsibility, I would be willing to hand over the world to them. I'm just afraid they're as smart as Xu You and won't come forward.

I want to retire. I feel, and I think most men can agree, that "having a son is enough to make one happy, and being without an official position makes one feel light." It is said that men are the masters of their own lives and the masters of the world, and the masters of their own souls and the masters of all human affairs; it is said that the best jobs in the world, such as being a civil official, a military general, a mayor, a judge, a director, or an editor-in-chief, are all monopolized by men. Honestly, who is happy about these things? The facts are very simple. A professor of psychology at Columbia University once said that the real division of labor between men and women is that men earn money and women spend it. I am very much in favor of switching things around. I would love to see women sweating in the docks, meeting rooms, editorial offices, and government offices, while we wear light-colored cheongsams in the garden, waiting for our loved ones to come out of the government offices and take us to the movies. Mrs. Heyne, with this wonderful idea, is truly lovely.

But let's put aside these selfish words. Honestly, when we look at our own governance record, we should be ashamed. Whether it's China or foreign countries, things can't be worse than they are now under the rule of men. So when the girls come to us and ask, "Let us womenfolk have a go," I can only honestly admit the failure of us men and hand over the power of the world to the womenfolk.

The womenfolk are good at giving birth to children, but we menfolk are bent on going to war and killing the best children. This is really called short-sightedness. But there's nothing we can do about it. It's in our nature. Men are always belligerent. Women at most pull hair and scratch faces at each other. If the wounds don't get infected, there's actually not much harm. Women at most fight each other with broomsticks, but men have to use machine guns against each other. Heywood Brown said that the problem is that we like to listen to gongs and drums, or modern military music. As long as we like to listen to gongs and drums, war will not be eliminated for a single day, this can be asserted. We can't resist the sound of gongs and drums. If women ruled the world and were about to declare war, then we could say, "Girls, the world is yours now. If you have to fight, go fight yourselves." Then no one would use machine guns against each other, and the world would truly be at peace.

We are really too shameless. The disarmament conference failed. The economic conference also failed. People, men, have failed. Everyone knows that the world should now ban poison gas and trade peacefully. But what are we doing? We don't invite contemporary sages such as Russell, Einstein, and Rolland to come out, but instead hand these matters over to "experts"! We want to reduce armaments and promote peace, but instead we invite a group of naval and military experts—killers with expertise in slaughter technology—to come to the meeting, and then we are shocked and surprised that the disarmament conference has failed. Later, everyone felt that war debts had to be canceled and tariffs had to be abolished in order for the global recession to end. What did we do? We invited some university professors, statisticians, and shortsighted "experts" who only know how to calculate percentages of tariffs to come to the meeting. And then we were shocked and surprised that the economic conference had also failed. Do you think these tariff experts would still have food to eat if tariffs were abolished? This is like inviting philology experts to come to a meeting to abolish Chinese characters.

Now I don't care about anything anymore. Diplomats are putting on white kidskin gloves and chatting with each other, but the clouds of war are spreading across the sky, and we are,

being clever. If we don't hurry up and take back the power to govern the world from the hands of white-gloved diplomats and thick-spectacled experts, there will soon be a great war, and everything will be over. So there's no need to worry too much about it. Therefore, when the womenfolk want to volunteer, I can only say, "Come on, girls! God bless you! Anyway, the results you achieve won't be worse than what we have now."

Honestly, governing the world is not very difficult, at least not as difficult as the "experts" tell us it is. If you want to ban poison gas, then ban poison gas. It can be done if you are sincere and if you don't invite "experts" to come to the meeting. Execute all the experts and invite George Bernard Shaw, Einstein, and Madame Curie to rule the world, and a second world war can and certainly will be avoided.

If monkeys knew about the things we humans are doing in Geneva, they would laugh their teeth out.

At least I myself am prepared to step down and hand over power to Tao Lao San, Fu Chun Lou Lao Liu, Zheng Yuxiu, and Zhang Mojun. Assuming I can save a little money, I want to run away to an island in the South Pacific or burrow into the mountains of Africa. If the likes of Fu Chun Lou Lao Liu still can't put an end to this disaster and European civilization is completely burned down, then I, living in a tree in the African jungle, can pat my chest and say, "God! At least I was honest."

How Do We Educate Children? 192

— A Traveler from Fukuoka

Seeing the mention of "Kong Yiji" reminded me of how China has always educated its children.

Nowadays, there are naturally all sorts of textbooks, but in village schools, there are still the "Three Character Classic" and the "Hundred Family Surnames." During the late Qing Dynasty, some people read the "Prodigy Poem," which boasted the glory of "scholars," with lines like "The emperor values heroes, writing is taught to you, all other occupations are inferior, only studying is noble." Some people read the "Young Student's Jewel Forest," which taught the clichés of classical Chinese prose with lines like "In the beginning of chaos, heaven and earth were established, the light and pure rose to become the sky, the heavy and turbid sank to become the earth." I don't know what came before that, but I heard that the "Taigong Family Instructions" were used during the late Tang and early Song dynasties, but they were lost for a long time, and were only later discovered in the Dunhuang caves. In the Han Dynasty, things like the "Jijiupian" were read.

Even so-called "textbooks" have changed so much in the last thirty years. Sometimes saying this, sometimes saying that, today's principles are like this, tomorrow's ideas are like that. Without adding "education," it's fine. But with "education" added, many people with internal contradictions are created from schools, and because of old social relationships, on the one hand, it's still the old fossil of "in the beginning of chaos, heaven and earth were established." China wants writers, wants "literary giants," but also wants true scholars. If someone were to write a history, making a clear record of the methods and books used to educate children throughout Chinese history, to let people understand how our ancestors, and even ourselves, were cultivated, then their merit would not be less than that of Yu (although he might just be a worm).

The contributors to "Free Talk" often include people who are learned in both ancient and modern times. I believe that there are many qualified people for this work. I wonder if anyone intends to do this? Bringing up this issue now is also knowing that it is easier said than done, so I can only speak empty words, hoping for strong proponents to develop it.

Child 193

— Zhou Lengjia

The child has been born for eight full months.

Round face, black eyes, plump white body, he smiles when he sees people, no one doesn't like him.

His wife especially loves him like something precious, holding him in the house all day long. She forgets about doing everything else.

But I hate him.

This fellow, ever since his mother had him, I've had bad luck: cocoons have fallen to twenty yuan per load, a hundred catties of grain is not worth two yuan, wheat and everything else has fallen in price, and I'm burdened with debt.

"Sell him," I often think: "We already have three sons, what do we need him for?"

And he's so good at acting spoiled, always crying for milk. The more he cries, the more awkward I feel, and I can't help but hit him. He cries even louder. My wife quickly comes over to pick him up, complaining to me:

"He didn't offend you, why are you hitting him for no reason?"

I often reply to her fiercely:

"You watch, one day I'll have to sell him."

Early this morning, as soon as I got out of bed, I heard him crying. I hated it so much, I ran outside like crazy. It was quiet outside, my wife had gone to wash rice, only the three sons were playing in the house. This was a good opportunity, I hurriedly picked him up and ran out the door.

As soon as I got out the door, I ran into my wife.

"Where are you taking him?" she stopped me and asked.

"To sell him, I don't want him in my house."

The rice sieve fell from my wife's hand, she rushed up to snatch him. But her strength was not as great as mine, I pushed her away with force and ran forward.

I stuck a straw tag on the child's head and shouted, "Selling a child!" I walked around the town all day.

No one paid attention to me. It started to rain. My stomach was hungry. I had no choice but to hold the child and go home.

As soon as I got home, I saw the three sons crying in the house, the rice sieve was still on the ground, but my wife was nowhere to be seen.

Several neighboring children told me a lot of bad news: some said she jumped into the river and died, some said she ran to the mountains, and some said they saw her running on the road, crying and shouting, "Give me back my child!"

I was stunned for a moment, my heart aching violently. I thought of my wife's many good qualities: how she shared my joys and sorrows, how she helped me maintain this family, how she took care of so many children...

"I have to bring her back." I said to myself, not bothering to put the child down in my hand, and ran out again.

It started to rain outside, pattering. The raindrops wet my clothes and body; they also wet the child's clothes and body. But I still ran in the rain regardless, shouting madly:

"Old Mother, where are you? Come back soon!"

There was no response, only the sound of raindrops pattering.

The child was also crying loudly in my arms.

Shanghai, Farewell! 194

— Yao Ke

After being sick, people often develop a special sensation in their mouths. No matter how delicious the dishes are, you know in your heart that it's good to eat, but as soon as it enters your mouth, it feels a bit strange -- tasteless!

In the past year or two, I have often had a special feeling in my spirit. This is not the fashionable "youth sickness" of boredom, because I have no economic pressure, nor am I suffering from unrequited love, and since I am alone in Shanghai, I certainly have no family problems. I do not dislike my work at all; in my spare time, I am very good at enjoying myself to the full; in terms of life, I can be considered a happy young man.

Normally, the "special feeling" I am talking about is subconscious, and I am not aware of its existence. However, it often floats into my consciousness like a dark cloud, without me realizing it. It does not necessarily lurk in my loneliness or boredom; often in moments of exhilaration, in the midst of busyness, I would feel as if I had been electrocuted, and in that instant, the exhilarating entertainment before me would become "tasteless."

People who have been sick often like to eat pickled cucumbers, salted radishes, and the like, to change their taste because their mouths are tasteless. I also want to change my taste -- Shanghai is really too greasy!

The train to Nanjing, full of stars, chased the cool night breeze westward. Ten minutes later, the skyline of this "greasy city" gradually disappeared into the dark night.

Shanghai, farewell!

Life and Machines 195

— Sun Yang

One

A reddish-brown steamer was moored at the Swire Wharf, a plume of black smoke rising from the chimney, standing straight up in the windless air; the soot, however, scattered and fell, sprinkling into the river and onto the heads of the coolies crowded on the wharf.

Most of the coolies were bare-chested, with gray-black cloths draped over their shoulders; their pants were patched with all sorts of patches, and were bound at the waist with moldy leather belts, blackened cloth belts, oily hemp ropes, or brand-new straw ropes. They stood in two uneven rows, filing into the belly of the great steamer through a small steel door. Those standing in the back craned their necks, anxiously looking forward, revealing an eagerness to go up immediately. But when they came out of the cabin, carrying packages that exceeded their own weight on their shoulders, they remembered that fatigue had already damaged every cell in their bodies: their thin, dark feet drew zigzag lines of unequal length, having long been unable to support even their thin, dark bodies. Beneath their disheveled hair, beads of sweat the size of soybeans rolled down their foreheads. Their dry, withered mouths sometimes opened suddenly, and "cough!" a mouthful of phlegm containing countless tuberculosis bacteria fell onto the floor.

The low pressure of the riverside in June penetrated into the gloomy cargo hold. Inside the hold, carbonic acid gas, the stench of sweat, and swirling dust, mixed with chaotic grunting sounds, penetrated into the coolies' nostrils, throats, and ears. However, the stench, the noise, and the distant home were all thrown to the back of their minds. Their only hope was that after the package was passed from the shoulders of the man coming from the lower hold by two strong men, it would be tossed a little lighter onto their shoulders.

The lower hold was lit by yellowish electric lights, which mixed with the grayish-white light leaking in from the staircase exit, faintly exuding a gloomy smell. Large packages were bound with iron bars, stacked layer upon layer on the floor. Dozens of machine-like animals, forgetting joy and happiness, labored in order in their weariness, like wheels driven by the same spring: four hands picked up a large package, placed it on another bare shoulder, and turned back to lift the second package; another pair of feet dragged their heavy steps, walking up the stairs to the left in their own grunting sounds, handing the heavy load over to the two strong men at the exit, and walking down to the right in the grunting sounds of others. This machine turned automatically, never stopping, and the goods flowed out of the exit like feces. If a part of the machine malfunctioned due to fatigue, then the bamboo whip in the hands of a person wearing a black gauze shirt replaced the lubricating oil, falling like raindrops on that part of the machine; thus, the wheel that had slipped its gears returned to the right track.

A thin, dark body carried a package, trudging up the stairs, his chest heaving with panting. The thin, dark, filthy flesh sank deeply, and the ribs were exposed like a model in a human anatomy museum. The dim light traced lines of shadow on them with the movements of the chest. The greasy pants barely covered the knees, and the two calves were exposed like tree branches in winter; with each step, the pair of knees shook as if paralyzed.

"Faster! Corpse! If you don't have the strength, don't eat this rice!" Such a roar was spat out from the top of the gauze shirt, and the bamboo whip whistled in the air, like a venomous snake seeking someone to bite. (To be continued)

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Markets Surge and Crash 196

Fluctuations Reach Ten Yuan, Falls Measure Nine Yuan

Commodity Prices, Exchange Rates, Silver Prices Continue to Open Lower, then Surge

White House's Inflationary Policy Remains Unchanged, then Sharply Declines

After several days of consecutive gains in the gold market, yesterday's morning session rose and then fell, dropping extremely rapidly. Although the afternoon market was low, it remained stable. Initially, foreign telegrams indicated that the British and American silver markets were falling, and exchange rates were also falling. The forward silver price on the metal exchange fell by 0.02, American wheat fell by 0.05, and American cotton fell by 0.19 pounds. Stocks fell by a small 2.19 yuan. The gross price initially opened at 77.78 yuan and continued to rise to over 80 yuan. After the customs closure, the initial situation showed an upward trend, with Qingfa Yongnu trying hard to buy in. After entering, the selling pressure surged to take advantage of the high prices, and the suppliers were unusually excited, resulting in a falling wind. The 80 yuan and 70 yuan marks were broken in quick succession. However, Reuters reported that the White House announced that the US government's inflationary policy had not changed its original intention, so the public believed that the authorities would continue to inflate the US dollar. Although this news was commonplace, since it was a government statement, it caused the gold market to fall back. After the afternoon close, it was once seen at 66-67 yuan. The afternoon market saw a sharp drop, so buyers surged, and the exchange rate market became more tense, stabilizing the situation. Bombay initially fell by 4 annas, then rose by 2 annas. After several consecutive narrow declines, today's fluctuations reached 20 yuan, which was a necessary reaction. Although Guangdong merchants sold, it was not as large as rumored. The cooked red price was increased by 175 yuan, and the swap spread was 6.5 yuan. The market conditions for today are recorded below:

The morning opening was 881.5 yuan, a rise of 6.3 yuan compared to the previous close. Goods opened at 1.3 yuan, and the exchange rate opened tight. The near-term selling price for British exchange was 1 shilling, 2 pence and 0.75, and the American exchange was 17.0625 yuan. Initially, prices hovered as banks successively supplied. By the time the October American dollar was difficult to settle at 0.375, goods from Yuanfeng, Yongheng, Zhifeng, Yongyuanmao, and Yongtongyi came in, and gradually rose from 0.05 yuan. Then, because the October American dollar was again difficult to settle at 0.3125, it rose to 4.2 yuan. Yongfeng sold off, and it became 2.2 yuan. Qingfa Yong came up and bought fiercely, and Dadecheng, Hengyu, Yuanmao, and Yong all bought in, and it rose to 5 yuan. Pan Gen came out with the November American dollar at 0.4375, Hengxing sold slightly and it fell. Huabi came out with the October dollar at 0.25, HSBC listed the British dollar down 0.125, the American dollar down 0.25. Fuyu, Daxing, and Yongyongfeng all sold, plus Hengxing and Hengtai vigorously sold. Huabi again blocked the October American dollar at 0.375, and it fell to 79 yuan. Yifeng and Yongyuanchun bought in on the dip, and the situation improved. Since the increase in tariffs, costs have suddenly increased, causing spot prices to suddenly soar. The small and large plaid rotten woolens that were sold for 1.1-2 yuan last year are now being sold by the industry for 2.25 yuan to 2.75 yuan. Compared with the new and old tariffs, the asking price is still flat. After all, the new goods of more than 2 yuan cannot reach the cost. There is a surge in the arrival of Melton goods, and old stocks are flooding the market. Those who have goods are selling at low prices. Yesterday, Taihe goods opened at 2.6 jiao and Guquanlong 2.5 jiao, and 豐 Yuanfeng opened at 2.55 jiao. It was found that the new and old goods of more than 2 yuan of rotten printed woolen fabrics are not many in stock. Those who hold the goods do not care about price reductions.

Essays

How to Remedy the Mental Illnesses of Young People 220

— Pu

Reading Mr. Erchu's "The Greatest Enemy of Young People's Psychology" in this publication, I cannot help but feel moved. Originally, I had been thinking about this issue for a long time and wanted to talk about it, but because the matter is significant, I dared not discuss it rashly. Now that someone has already talked about it first and hopes to arouse resonance, I will also "attach myself to the end" and say a few words, contributing a little humble opinion.

Upon investigation, the reason why young people have psychological problems is, of course, that they do not have a firm will or accurate rationality. However, the other aspects of family, school, and society cannot be held responsible, because the good or bad environment, the completeness or lack of education, and the righteousness or wickedness of the career are all greatly related to the psychology of young people. Now, how to remedy the psychological problems of young people? Naturally, simply saying that young people should extricate themselves and how to save themselves will probably be difficult to achieve effective results. At the very least, it is necessary to unite the family, school, and society in various aspects, dividing labor and cooperating in order to achieve even a slight effect.

(1) Young people themselves:

A. Understand the responsibility of being a "person" and determine one's own "outlook on life."

B. Organize one's own thoughts and develop a logical mind.

C. Forge one's own will and strive for the goals to be achieved.

D. Embrace a spirit of perseverance and excellence to cope with adverse environments.

E. Sanction improper desires and recognize that "personality" and "knowledge" are the weapons to transform everything. F. Resist all inherited forces and establish one's own life.

G. Develop a spirit of mutual assistance to unite and support other young people.

(2) Family aspect:

A. Provide appropriate guidance on the lives of young people.

B. Give young people the right to freedom of marriage.

C. Recognize that young people have a considerable position in the family.

D. Encourage young people to develop independent abilities.

(3) School aspect:

A. Promote vocational education so that young people who cannot further their studies have the skills to make a living. B. Implement mass education so that out-of-school young people have the opportunity to acquire knowledge. C. Focus on sex education so that young people do not go astray.

D. Guide young people on various methods of self-cultivation.

E. Find ways to improve the poor environment of young people.

(4) Social aspect:

A. Develop production businesses to accommodate the surplus of young people in the workforce.

B. Reform the private property system so that the environment for young people is gradually equalized.

C. Eliminate all inherited forces that bind the thoughts of young people in religion and customs. D. Organize legitimate entertainment venues so that young people have suitable leisure activities.

E. Establish a youth savings bank to cultivate young people's savings habits.

F. Establish a youth unemployment agency to prevent young people from drifting and falling.

G. Publish youth publications to take on the responsibility of guidance and assistance.

H. Hold public lectures on ethics and academics to awaken young people from time to time.

Dear young people! The youth problem is related to the entire problem of society. I am very ashamed to ask myself that I have not conducted detailed observations on the practical aspects of society. Now, due to the limited space, the remedy plan is written very simply, and there are bound to be many superficial points. Please do not hesitate to add to the discussion.

Tricks in the Evening 221

— Tu Ma

I remember there are two old poems, "The sunset is infinitely good, it's just near dusk", one sentence describes the beauty of the sunset, and the other sentence laments that after the sunset, it will be dark. But when the weather is hot, especially in Shanghai, where there are many people in small houses, they are oppressed by the heat all day long, as if they are trapped in a steamer. They have no money and no good fortune to escape the summer. They only hope that the violent sun will set earlier. What else are they interested in seeing the scenery of the sunset? And I hope that a rain and a few gusts of wind will make everyone feel refreshed. What mood do they have to care about darkness and light?

The foundation of life is built on money, which is a fact that everyone cannot deny. The performers, of course, cannot escape this example. They rely on a few sets of "deceptive tricks" to find some money to maintain their food and clothing, as well as the lives of "dogs and monkeys". Taking advantage of the late day and the slight breeze, they lead the dogs and monkeys, carry wooden boxes on their backs, and honestly and impolitely hang up a few "masks" and run to the streets to develop their way to make money.

At this time, many people are sitting and standing by the roadside wall. Although the heat has not subsided, these people are already preparing to enjoy the coolness that nature gives them. If there is a larger open space nearby, then it is regarded as the "Kuling of the laborers", the "Qingdao, Mogan Mountain for the poor". Regardless of men, women, old and young, they all go to the open space to rest and cool off until late at night before dispersing.

The sound of the small gong rang loudly, and naturally many people gathered to join in the fun, forming a circle and surrounding the two performers, a dog, and a monkey in the middle to watch them perform tricks.

The dog and the monkey began to work. "The dog walks in circles", and the monkey is already wearing a red cloth shirt, but unfortunately he is not wearing trousers. At this time, the performer gave an order, and the dog walked even faster. "The monkey also puts on a mask" and a "broken gauze hat" on his head, vividly playing the old tricks of what the common saying calls "dressed beasts", which only made a group of ignorant and uneducated children happy to dance.

The sky gradually darkened, and the performer's bag was filled with a lot of copper coins. He excitedly led the dog and the monkey away. I only heard the people who were cooling off say: The dog and the monkey were only willing to listen to the performer's orders because of the "problem of food". To teach the monkey to perform tricks, you must first "kill the chicken to show the monkey". The monkey is afraid of death, so he learns it. However, the dog and the monkey do not understand what tricks they are learning and doing, "just being manipulated by others".

What Kind of Logic Is This? 222

— Shi Ben

Mosquitoes buzzed, their wings fluttering as they formed ranks and began their campaign of aggression. It was a hot summer evening, and the bedroom was simply unbearable due to their disturbances. Left with no choice, I temporarily emulated Young Marshal Zhang's policy of non-resistance and retreated from the entire bedroom, seeking coolness on the street outside the gate, temporarily avoiding their onslaught.

Once outside, the streetlights shone with a brilliance like a painting. These ferocious and cruel Red Bandits (mosquitoes – full of red terror), dared not brazenly launch a full-scale attack, but instead covertly broke into smaller units to steal some vitamins from behind.

What? What is this? Why are these people rushing westward, some with tense expressions? Could there be a fire somewhere? But I don't hear anyone shouting "Fire!" What exactly is going on? A quick look would reveal the answer; what need is there to overthink it, idiot? So, I stood up and aimlessly followed the crowd. After walking past a dozen or so storefronts, I gleaned from their discussions that the local Public Security Bureau had just caught four opium offenders on East Street, and they were about to be interrogated immediately, and the crowd was going to watch the proceedings. Arresting opium users is a common occurrence, what's so interesting about that? But in this 18th-century town, novelty is rare.

Page 20

After dinner, with no movie theaters to provide entertainment, going to watch the opium offenders being interrogated wasn't necessarily a bad way to pass the time, so their actions should be forgiven.

"Are you selling opium?" "Officer, I wouldn't dare sell it!" "Nonsense! There are four opium pipes and a jar of opium. The evidence is irrefutable, how dare you deny it?" "Yes..." "Why do you three smoke opium?" ("Officer, we wouldn't dare smoke it!" "You've been caught red-handed, how dare you quibble?" "Yes, yes, yes...") I stood in the crowd and heard this exchange. At the same time, I craned my neck to look inside and saw four bloodless killing devices (opium lamps) and a black-stained ceramic jar on the table. Presumably, it contained the utterly evil opium. The interrogation of the opium offenders was swift. Look, they’d all confessed with just a few words from each of them.

"These four addicts have been caught red-handed, their confessions are clear, so the Public Security Bureau will, according to the law, detain them for a maximum of twenty-four hours, and undoubtedly transfer them to the court tomorrow. The outcome will likely be a sentence of at least three months to a year of imprisonment for each of them. Given their long-standing habits, their punishment might even be more severe. It seems everyone should be law-abiding and not commit crimes, knowing that as the saying goes, 'The prince who breaks the law is judged the same as a commoner.' The majesty and sanctity of the law cannot be circumvented by anyone!" A person thought to themself on the way home.

The next day, going out into the street, what a surprise! How come the four opium offenders arrested by the Public Security Bureau last night have already been released? They are still walking around on the street, not going to court at all? The limits of legal judgment that I speculated about in my mind on the way home last night are absolutely contrary to reality. Has the law lost its authority and effectiveness? Otherwise, why would these four opium offenders who were caught red-handed with irrefutable confessions be free and not subject to legal judgment? Truly strange!

Calligraphy and Paintings by Contemporary Celebrities 223

Landscape by Mr. Yu Xiaolian (Brief Biography)

Yu Xiaolian is a native of Songjiang, Jiangsu. He possessed innate talent in calligraphy and painting, and by the age of thirteen, he had already astonished his elders. The epigrapher Fei Longding especially valued him, treating him like a young friend, frequently visiting him for discussions and enjoyment, which furthered his artistic progress. His landscape paintings are reminiscent of Dong Yuan, Ju Ran, and the Four Wangs, while his figures and flower paintings are inspired by Chen Hongshou and Xu Wei. Longding presented him with a poem containing the line, "Who can continue the Huating school of painting? Clouds and mists arise before his eyes from Ruifeng," which is indeed a fitting compliment. This particular painting slightly incorporates the strength and elegance of Huang Gongwang's style, and his knowledge of epigraphy and poetry is also quite refined.

Novel: War and Peace (2) 224

— Ling He

Middle-aged man: What's there to be afraid of? Even if we don't burn it ourselves, the Japanese soldiers will burn it.

Child: Great, the planes are gone, we can go out now.

Old woman: Let's hide for a little longer, they might come back.

Old man: (Coming out of the cave first) Hmph, I managed to hide and avoid death again. In times like these, alas, it's better to be dead!

(The people in the cave come out one after another, the woman holding a child in her arms, and leading another larger one.)

Woman: Alright, let's go back, I wonder if the wheat bran is burnt.

(The one she is leading refuses to go, because he sees someone pasting paper on the wall, and there is also a soldier posting a notice. The woman goes alone.

Child: Mom, I'll go in a little while.

(The soldier finishes posting the notice on the temple wall and leaves, everyone gathers around to look. One of them reads it slowly.)

Middle-aged man: "Resisting Japan and killing the enemy is the Central Government's top priority. Not only saving the country, but loving the villagers. Killing the enemy to achieve results, disregarding death. Fighting hard day and night, the enemy's morale is faltering. The people love and protect them, offering baskets of food and pots of drink. Discipline is strict, not disturbing the locals. Unanimously supporting, enhancing national glory..."

Old man: What is it talking about, I can't understand a word.

Middle-aged man B: I don't understand either. Hey! (Asking the one reading the notice) Is this a notice from our Chinese government? Does it mention airplanes?

Middle-aged man: No.

Middle-aged man B: Then the southern soldiers? Does it mention whether they are coming or not?

Middle-aged man: No.

Old man: Then what exactly does this notice say?

Middle-aged man: Didn't I read it? It says how good the Central Government's soldiers are. But I don't understand what that means.

Old woman: The Japanese soldiers also dropped a lot of leaflets from the planes, saying how good they are. Everyone says they are good, but I don't know who to believe.

Middle-aged man: No matter what, saying it's good is useless. Whichever army is really willing to fight the Japanese desperately is a good army. We don't need them to teach us to support them, and we will naturally support them. Grandpa! (pointing at the old man) Are you right? As long as they don't make us slaves to a foreign country, we are willing to do anything.

Old man: Isn't that right? Since the Republic, there have been years of chaos and war, we have suffered so many disasters, and now if they are really willing to fight foreigners, what's wrong with suffering again?

Middle-aged man C: If we're not contributing to the country, then Heaven must have no eyes. For example, yesterday I wasn't at home, and one of my donkeys and a mule were taken by the soldiers to transport things. If I were at home, of course I would have gone with them. Now who knows where they went? But my whole family relies on these two animals to make a living. I waited all afternoon in one area, hoping they would come back so I could take them back. But they still haven't come back, it's driving me crazy.

Movie Special

The Defensive Line of British Films 225

— Bai Zu

Absorption and Renovation of the Nanking Theater

The dominance of American films in the Chinese market undoubtedly sparked strong resistance from German films. In every major city in China, we see the invasion and activity of German films. At the same time, British films are also closely following, introducing several "British Style" song and dance films one after another, such as "Camp Meeting," "Happy Go Lucky," and "Nightingale." However, British films did not have a sufficient outlet behind them, and relying on theaters could not achieve satisfactory development. Therefore, they used their skills and leased the Nanking Theater, which occupies a corner of the Meiersi Ai Road, forming the first defensive line.

The agent for British films is British Films Company. They have a considerable understanding with domestic filmmakers. Several famous film companies have signed long-term contracts, continuously supplying them with films that they believe suit the tastes of Chinese audiences. Not only that, but they also sent a formal representative, Chang Chuan, to reside in London and be responsible for this matter. It is said that in the past two years, the development of the British film industry has indeed made significant progress, both in terms of technology and performance. They first improved the quality, followed by enriching the entertainment elements, aiming to create films with considerable entertainment connotations. The several films that have been released in this area in the past are the initial products under this standard. Of course, they hope to have more exceptional works that surpass everything that Hollywood has contributed.

Indeed, musical comedies from Britain have achieved great success in both domestic and foreign markets, so filmmakers are even more determined to promote "entertainment" as a slogan, increasing the production of such musicals. Coming soon to be released in this area is "Marry Me," starring Lana Morris, the star of "Happy Go Lucky," which is a lighthearted comedy. There are also two films starring Jack Hulbert, who played the old servant in "Happy Go Lucky": "Jack's the Boy" and "Hove on Wheels." His novel and humorous performance is most worthy of people's memory. Alexander Korda is a leading expert in making comedies. He specially selected two difficult-to-portray and cold-humored comedians, Roland Young and George Grossmith, to star in "Wedding Rehearsal," offering something new and special. "Rome Express" is a great all-star work, with the same significance as Hollywood's "Grand Hotel," which deserves our deep attention.

For the arrival of these new films, the movie palace where they will premiere, the Nanking Theater, has also undergone special internal and external renovations. The seats have been completely renovated, and the sound system uses the latest type from Western Electric. This machinery can avoid all echoes while amplifying the lowest sounds and reducing the highest sounds. Their only goal is to allow people who have worked hard to step into this movie palace and feel spiritual inspiration and inexplicable comfort.

Xu Xinfu: A New Lease on Life After Disaster 226

"Giant Port of the East" to Hit the Screen

Since completing "Blood Debt," Xu Xinfu had not worked for a long time. Recently, he received a script set against the backdrop of a salt field, "Salt Tide," and immediately his tepid enthusiasm rose to a boil, and he began work. The other day, he led a team including Hu Die, Wang Xianqi, Sun Min, Gu Meijun, and others, smiling happily to Shangganpu to shoot exterior scenes. Unexpectedly, in the evening he received an urgent letter from the salt field in that area, saying that recent storms and raging waves had caused the collapse of the thatched sheds along the coast, and so everyone in the company thought they would go there full of excitement, and return with disappointment. However, yesterday the company's two cars returned, saying that as soon as they arrived in Ganpu, the storm stopped and the raging waves subsided. Therefore, Xu Xinfu, like someone with "a new lease on life after disaster," happily began working.

Film Review

Review of "Pick Up" 227

— Ling He

Generally speaking, American films are almost always produced under a fixed formula, and this is something that we can see again in "Pick Up."

The young woman, Mary, is implicated in a crime because of her bad husband and is imprisoned. After her ex-husband is released from prison, she is unable to maintain a living. Fortunately, she meets a young chauffeur, and through his introduction, she becomes a telephone operator at a car dealership. Later, the chauffeur, encouraged by the advice of a woman with no connections, strives to improve himself and eventually becomes the owner of a small car dealership. His life is now prosperous, unlike in the past. The chauffeur wants to marry the woman, but she refuses because she is already committed to someone else. Soon after, he begins to associate with a romantic woman. Seeing this situation, the woman decisively asks a lawyer for a divorce from her husband. The chauffeur then proposes to his romantic woman, but is also rejected. At this time, the woman's husband is released from prison and threatens to kill the chauffeur, forcing the woman to go with him. In the end, the woman cleverly reports to the police and has her divorced husband arrested. With the chauffeur's utmost help, she is able to live happily ever after with her true love.

In this story, it is easy to find many points that are the same as other films. In order to write about a woman who is faithful to love, it is necessary to write about the other party (the man) not being dedicated to love, being fickle, or being bewitched by another woman, so there must be a tramp appearing in the story. To write about a chaste woman changing her mind, it must be because she met the wrong person and was forced to remarry, so there must be a villainous bandit appearing in the story. Finally, to illustrate that true love between a man and a woman must be obtained through hardship, after several twists and turns, the sentimental men and women end up together under the protection of the law. This is a formula on the screen, most applicable to American films. The Tianyi Film Company in China has a new sound film called "Vitality," directed by Shao Zuiweng and starring Chen Yumei.

Film producers, in order to "learn from the skills of their predecessors," try their best to adopt this formula. This formula has been reflected in many works in China, and it is probably unnecessary to provide examples.

Some people say that American films can only circle around romance, and this is indeed a proof of the fact. However, the scope of romance is not necessarily so small. Can't they come up with some new tricks? Therefore, on the one hand, they feel a lack of subject matter to the extreme, (in fact, if the writer's life is rich, they will never have this feeling). On the other hand, they can't help but feel powerless when they repeatedly fabricate stories.

Because of the stale and uninteresting story, no matter how hard the director works, they cannot make this film have any value. The director's ability, at best, is that he can make the performance quite interesting, and the result is to make people laugh with the dialogue. However, the monotony of the performance is also unavoidable due to the story. In the first half, we only see the male and female protagonists walking on the screen. Even though the dialogue is funny, it cannot arouse the audience's interest. Although it becomes quite tense later on, due to the fragmented sub-scenes, it ultimately fails to organize the audience's emotions. Perhaps some small details are commendable, such as the heroine returning from her divorce with extreme joy, but unable to gain the love of her lover, the scene of the romantic woman's joy, and the heroine's clever reporting to the police, but in the end, it cannot obtain its special value because of this.

Sylvia Sidney received a lot of praise from Chinese people for playing "Madame Butterfly," but like the director, she could not maintain her past achievements in this film. Of course, the tone of "Pick Up" and "Madame Butterfly" are completely different, but the personality of the character she plays is still not much different. It can be seen that actors cannot succeed in the same range.

As an aside, this work did not receive good reviews in Japan either. The film title was translated as "Pavement," which is certainly not as tempting as the Chinese translation, but I wonder if it is appropriate to translate it directly as "Choice"?

On the Popularization of Cinema 228

— Ren Ying

The popularization of cinema is truly shouted loudly this year, while at the same time the popularization of cinema is also misunderstood by the general public. And the starting point of why cinema should be popularized, there are roughly two reasons: (1) To rely on cinema to educate the public, to supplement the inadequacy of public education. (2) To bring the painful moans of the times to the screen, so that people know what kind of era it is now. This is like the popularization of literature and art, so that the ladies and wives of the city, after watching sweet and loving romance films, are instilled with images of the suffering masses, or to change their tastes.

Regarding the popularization of cinema, many people have published theories in this area in the past. In fact, the popularization of cinema is not about the national film industry unanimously mobilizing and specializing in using popular themes to describe popular films. Otherwise, it is not possible in practice, and such work is also unnecessary. Popular films only need to be able to move people; this is more powerful than words. In short, popular films should use the consciousness of the times to shout out the moans of the masses. Or educate the public and give them a new inspiration.

I remember a certain film publication, regarding the popularization of cinema, once published a satire that was as humorous as George Bernard Shaw. It said: "If the popularization of cinema is suitable for the present, we can call the bums on the road to be actors. And compile scripts such as 'The Love History of a Rickshaw Puller', 'The Scandalous History of a Thatched Shed', etc..." (Because the original text is not available, I remember it roughly as above.) I think these are not only groundless satires from a certain film publication, or they can be considered a misunderstanding. This is still the general misunderstanding of the popularization of cinema today. We certainly hope that the popularization of cinema can achieve the effect of educating the public in the future; it is not about turning the lives of the public into decadent lives, and moving it to the screen. I hope that friends who study the popularization of cinema will have a strong response.

Chen Yumei's records released by Baidai Company. There are "Lullaby", "Swallows Fly in Pairs", "Flowers Tease the Shadow", "Frugality Song", "For Modern Misses", etc. Because Chen Yumei's singing has a quiet and gentle charm, which is very different from others. Now, the first new song "Little Baby" has also been recorded by Baidai Company and has already begun to be released.

Movie Novel: The Morning Glory (10) 230

— Ma Zhan

Sheridan and Easton were arguing indecisively when they heard the door of the opposite bedroom open. Eve Lowell was humming the lyrics of "Romeo and Juliet" and walking out quickly. Sheridan hurried after her, but when he saw her, he didn't get a chance to give her the money in the envelope. She just kept talking about her infatuation with Easton, saying she didn't have time and wanted to plan her future collaboration with Easton alone. She said it wasn't because Easton's position in the theater was high now, but she really wanted to help him because she thought Easton was too good. After she finished speaking, she held out her hand to say goodbye to Sheridan and left. Sheridan stood there blankly for a while and then left, unwilling to see Easton for the time being.

Like a happy dream, wings sprout and fly to the highest clouds; but when the dream wakes and disappears, what you feel is the stinging pain in your chest. The wings are also broken, beating in the piercing cold wind, and pitifully must eventually fall. At first, Eve was stubbornly unwilling to believe she would be disappointed, but long-term starvation and cold forced her to accept the theory of fate. But she can still try to move forward, holding her head high, her eyes facing upwards, enduring the pain of the new wounds on her heart, still wanting to chase the fleeting hope. As for Easton, this matter has also been left behind with Eve's disappearance. All the things that don't go through the heart are forgotten after a while. The days pass quickly, the rehearsal date for "Blue Sky" is coming to an end, and "Golden Branch" is being rehearsed. Rita Vernon haughtily looks down on everything. Her friends, who usually flatter her, compliment her every day, telling her that the success of "Blue Sky" is entirely due to her outstanding talent, and that she should receive double the salary and a portion of the surplus profits. She believed this deeply, waiting for the opportunity to come. She knew that Sheridan was against her playing the lead role in "Golden Branch," but

She forced Easton to give her the lead role. Sheridan knew that Rita didn't understand the plot and was afraid that it wouldn't be easy to fool the audience, but Rita's absolute confidence made him helpless. Rita's sudden outburst made her despise all standards of comparison, thinking she was the only great female lead of her time. She now saw that a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity had arrived. She had made a plan in her mind, waiting for the first night of the opening of "Golden Branch" so that she could propose her conditions to Easton, forcing Easton to admit it, so that he would be caught off guard and had no choice but to surrender unconditionally. When she was arranging this, she did not think that Sheridan had already made preparations. During the rehearsal process of "Golden Branch," Sheridan watched silently from the sidelines. Rita completely ignored his instructions. Her identity was completely inconsistent with the identity of the character in the play. While Sheridan lamented that the plot could not be developed faithfully, he was thinking of finding a suitable lead and rearranging "Golden Branch." (To be continued)
